When your operation is complete, then fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine; then treat it with the remaining care until it heals.

¶ De cura Ramicis, quae est cum Vite.  
On the treatment of Varicocele, which occurs with a swelling.

Caput LXIIII.  
Chapter 64.

Uitis est apostema inuolutum quadam inuolutione, simile botro, cum mollificatione testiculorum: et fit difficilis super infirmum motus et exercitium, et deambulatio.  
The swelling is an abscess enveloped in a certain layer, resembling a cluster of grapes, along with the softening of the testicles, and it makes movement, exercise, and walking difficult for the patient.

Et in curatione huius aegritudinis est ex timore, propter illud cuius praecessit rememoratio.  
And in the treatment of this condition, there is a need for caution due to what has been previously mentioned.

Verum oportet, ut dicamus operationem in ea secundum quod fecerunt primi.  
But it is necessary that we describe the operation as the ancients performed it.

Dico ergo, quod oportet ut facias sedere infirmum super sedem eleuatam.  
I say, therefore, that you must make the patient sit on an elevated seat.

Deinde impelle suspensorium testiculorum ad inferiora.  
Then, push the suspensory ligament of the testicles downward.

Deinde tene cutem testiculorum cum digitis tuis, cum uasis quae sunt propinqua uirgae: et teneat ea minister alius, et extendat ea extensione uehementi.  
Then, hold the skin of the testicles with your fingers, along with the vessels near the penis; and another assistant should hold and stretch them with a strong extension.

Deinde incide cum spatumili lato acuto sectione transuersa in directo uasorum, donec detegantur uasa.  
Then cut with a broad, sharp blade, making a transverse incision in line with the vessels until the vessels are exposed.

Deinde excoria ab omni parte, sicut diximus tibi in extractione Arteriarum quae sunt in timporibus.  
Then strip away from every part, as we described to you in the extraction of the arteries in the temples.

Postea fige in eis acum in qua sit filum duplum, et liga ipsum in primo locorum quibus accidunt Vites: et liga ipsum iterum in ultimo eorum.  
Afterwards, insert a needle with a doubled thread into them, and tie it at the first place where the swellings occur, and tie it again at the end of these locations.

Deinde seca ea in media sectione recta secundum longitudinem corporis, et extrahe quod aggregatur ex humiditatibus faeculentis corruptis.  
Then cut them in the middle with a straight incision along the body's length and extract the accumulated foul and corrupted fluids.

Deinde cura uulnus cum curatione reliquorum uulnerum, in quibus uis generari saniem, ut cadant uasa quae nutriunt unum testiculorum.  
Then treat the wound with the same treatment as for other wounds where you wish to produce suppuration so that the vessels which nourish one of the testicles are severed.

Non est enim malum per illud.  
For it is not harmful because of this.

Si autem accidat Vitis omnibus uasis, tunc oportet ut extrahantur propter hoc testiculi cum uasis: ut non priuetur ouum nutrimento, propter incisionem, et tabescat, uel arescat, et non sit iuuamentum cum eis.  
But if the swelling affects all the vessels, then it is necessary to remove the testicles along with the vessels, so that the testicle is not deprived of nourishment, which would cause it to waste away, or dry up, and there would be no benefit in keeping them.

¶ De cura Ramicis intestinalis.  
On the treatment of intestinal rupture.

Caput LXV.  
Chapter 65.

Euentus huius Ramicis est ex sectione, quae accidit in sifach extenso super uentrem in parte inguinum ex mirach uentris.  
The occurrence of this rupture is from a cut, which happens in the membrane stretched over the abdomen in the area of the groin from the lower abdomen.

Quare descendunt intestina ex illa Ruptura ad unum testiculorum.  
Therefore, the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the testicles.

Et haec Ruptura est aut ex sifach, aut extensione eius.  
And this rupture is either from the membrane or its extension.

Et accidunt istae duae species ex caussis multis: aut ex percussione, aut saltu, aut clamore, aut eleuatione rei grauis, et similibus.  
And these two types happen for many reasons: either from a blow, a jump, a shout, lifting a heavy object, and similar causes.

Et signum, quando est ex extensione sifach.  
And the sign, when it is from the extension of the membrane.

Est quod accidit paulatim in tempore longo, et non accidit subito: et est apostema aequale uersus profundum: propterea, quod sifach comprimit intestinum.  
Is that it happens gradually over a long time, and does not happen suddenly: and it is a swelling equally towards the depth, because the membrane compresses the intestine.

Et signum eius quando est ex sectione sifach, quia facit accidere ex principio sui dolorem uehementem subito: et est apostema diuersum, apparens sub cute propinque: et illud est propter exitum intestini, et cursus eius ad exteriora sifach.  
And the sign of it when it is from a cut in the membrane is that it causes intense pain suddenly from its beginning: and it is a swelling, irregular, appearing close under the skin: and this is due to the exit of the intestine, and its movement to the exterior of the membrane.

Et quandoque egreditur cum intestino zirbum: et nominatur haec Ramex intestinalis, et zirbia: et quandoque fit cum uentositate.  
And sometimes a zirbum comes out with the intestine: and this is called an intestinal rupture and zirbia: and sometimes it occurs with wind.

Et quandoque currit in intestinum stercus, et retinetur illic: et est cum eo pernicies infirmi: quoniam facit accidere dolorem prauum, et praecipue quando premitur.  
And sometimes feces move into the intestine and are retained there: and with this is harm to the patient, since it causes severe pain, especially when pressed.

Et in curatione specierum aegritudinis huius cum ferro est timor: quare oportet ut caueatur casus in ea.  
And in the treatment of this type of illness with surgery, there is danger; therefore, it is necessary to be cautious of complications in it.

Et modus operationis est, ut praecipias infirmo, ut reducat intestinum manu sua ad interiora concauitatis suae, si obedit reditui.  
And the method of operation is that you instruct the patient to return the intestine with his hand to the interior of its cavity, if it will respond to being returned.

Deinde resupinetur super collum suum inter manus tuas: et eleua crura eius.  
Then he is to be laid back on his neck between your hands, and his legs are lifted.

Deinde extende cutem quae sequitur cutem ad superiora, et seca cutem testiculorum totam per longitudinem.  
Then stretch the skin that follows the skin upwards, and cut the entire skin of the testicles along its length.

Deinde fige in duobus labiis sectionis uncinos, secundum quod indiges ad aperiendum sectionem cum eis: et sectio sit secundum quantitatem, quod sit possibile, ut egrediatur ex ea ouum.  
Then fix hooks into the two lips of the incision, as you need to open the incision with them; and let the incision be to such a size that it is possible for an egg to come out of it.

Deinde excoria siphak, et quae sunt sub cute testiculorum, donec quando detegitur sifach album, durum ab omni parte: tunc intromitte digitum tuum indicem in eo quod sequitur testiculum, in eo quod est inter siphach album, quod est sub cute oui, et inter sifach secundum, et absolue cum eo adhaerentiam quae est in posteriori parte oui.  
Then scrape away the membrane, and what is under the skin of the testicles, until the white membrane is revealed, hard on all sides; then insert your index finger into the area that follows the testicle, in that which is between the white membrane under the skin of the egg and the second membrane, and release with it the adhesion which is on the back part of the egg.

Deinde moue cum manu dextra ad interiora cutem testiculorum: et cum hoc extende sifach album ad sursum, cum manu sinistra: et eleua ouum cum sifach ad partem sectionis: et praecipe ministro, ut extendat ouum ad sursum: et tu solue adhaerentiam, quae est retro solutione completa.  
Then move with your right hand the skin of the testicles inward; and with this, extend the white membrane upward with your left hand: and lift the egg with the membrane toward the side of the incision: and instruct your assistant to extend the egg upward: and you release the adhesion, which is at the back, with complete separation.

Et quaere digitis tuis, ut non sit aliquid illic ex intestino inuoluto in sifach albo duro.  
And check with your fingers that there is nothing there from the intestine wrapped in the hard white membrane.

Si autem inuenis ex eo aliquid: tunc impelle ipsum ad uentrem inferius.  
If, however, you find anything of it, then push it back towards the lower abdomen.

Deinde accipe acum, in qua sit filum grossum, factum licinium ex decem filis: et intromitte ipsam apud postremum sifach, id est, tunicae, quod est sub cute testiculorum quae sequitur sectionem: deinde incide extremitates quae eminent ex filo, donec sint quatuor fila.  
Then take a needle, in which there is a thick thread, made of linen from ten threads: and insert it at the base of the membrane, that is, the tunic which is under the skin of the testicles that follows the incision: then cut the ends that extend from the thread, until there are four threads.

Deinde compone quaedam eorum super quaedam cum figura quae sit in modo crucis: et liga cum eis alsifach, de quo diximus, quia est sub cute testiculorum ligamento uehementi, donec non possit aliquod ex uasis, quae nutriunt eos mittere ad eos aliquid: ut non accidat inde apostema calidum.  
Then arrange some of them over others in a shape like a cross: and tie the membrane, of which we spoke, that is under the skin of the testicles with a strong ligature, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can send anything to them, so that a warm swelling does not occur from there.

Et pone iterum ligamentum secundum extra ligamentum primum, longinquum ab eo minus duobus digitis.  
And again place a second ligature outside the first ligature, two fingers away from it.

Et post ista duo ligamenta dimitte ex sifach, quod est sub cute testiculorum, quantitatem magnitudinis digiti: et incide reliquum totum secundum rotunditatem, et aufer ex eo ouum.  
And after these two ligatures, leave a portion of the membrane under the skin of the testicles, the size of a finger’s breadth, and cut the rest completely around, and remove the egg from it.

Deinde seca in inferiori parte cutis testiculorum sectione, ex qua currit sanguis, et sanies: sicut narrauimus in eo quod praemissum est.  
Then cut in the lower part of the skin of the testicles at the incision, from which blood and serum flow, as we described in what was previously stated.

Deinde administra lanam submersam in oleo, et pone in uulnus: et administra ligamentum quod narrauimus.  
Then apply wool soaked in oil, and place it on the wound: and apply the bandage which we described.

Et quandoque cauterizatur sifach album quod diximus, post incisionem eius timendo de fluxu sanguinis.  
And sometimes the white membrane, as we said, is cauterized after its incision to prevent blood flow.

Multotiens enim accidit illud.  
For it often happens.

Et dimitte ligamentum, donec cadat per se.  
And leave the bandage until it falls off on its own.

Si autem tardatur casus eius, tunc embrocetur cum aqua calida: et pone super ipsum illud quod diximus, donec cadat.  
If it takes too long to fall off, then bathe it with warm water: and place on it what we said, until it falls.

Deinde cura uulnus cum reliqua curatione uulnerum, donec curetur.  
Then treat the wound with the remaining treatment for wounds, until it is healed.

¶ De Ramice uentosa.  
On a windy rupture.

Caput LXVI.  
Chapter 66.

IN Hac Ramice non uidi aliquem qui ausus fuerit super curationem eius cum ferro.  
In this rupture, I have not seen anyone who dared to treat it with surgery.

Et primi quidem dixerunt, quod fit sicut narrauimus in Ramice quae est cum Vite.  
And the first ones indeed said that it is done as we described in the rupture that involves the scrotum.

Quod est, ut liges uasa post sectionem super ea cum facilitate inferius: deinde seca in medio, et cura postremo cum eo quod aperit ipsum, donec cadant uasa: et cura uulnus, secundum quod diximus, donec sanetur.  
That is, to tie the vessels below the section with ease: then cut in the middle, and finally treat it with what opens it until the vessels fall away: and treat the wound, as we said, until it is healed.

¶ De disruptione quae fit in inguinibus.  
On the rupture that occurs in the groin.

Caput LXVII.  
Chapter 67.

Quando accidit Ruptura in inguinibus, sicut diximus, et eminet locus, et non descendit ad testiculos aliquid ex intestinis: et si descendit, est illud parum, et redit in omnibus horis: uerum si prolongatur cum ea tempus, additur fissura in sifach, donec descendunt intestina in sifach.  
When a rupture occurs in the groin, as we said, and the area swells, and nothing of the intestines descends to the testicles; and if something descends, it is little, and it returns every hour. But if time is prolonged with it, a tear is added in the membrane, until the intestines descend into the membrane.

Et accidit illud ex extensione sifach, quod est in inguinibus, sicut diximus.  
And this happens from the extension of the membrane, which is in the groin, as we said.

Quod est, quia extenditur sifach: deinde mollificatur, et apostematur locus, et eminet.  
That is, because the membrane is stretched: then it softens, the area swells, and it protrudes.

Et cura eius est cum cauterio, sicut praecessit eius narratio.  
And its treatment is with cautery, as previously narrated.

Et quandoque curatur cum ferro, secundum hunc modum: et est, ut iaceat infirmus super dorsum suum inter manus tuas.  
And sometimes it is treated with surgery, in the following way: that the patient should lie on his back between your hands.

Deinde seca locum Rupturae apostematum et eminentem, sectione per latitudinem, secundum quantitatem trium digitorum.  
Then cut the swollen and protruding rupture site, with an incision across it the width of three fingers.

Deinde stringe alsifak et, quae sunt sub cute, donec quando detegitur sifach album, quod est sub cute quae sequitur ipsum.  
Then tie the membrane and what is under the skin, until the white membrane, which is under the skin that follows it, is revealed.

Tunc accipe radium, et pone ipsum super locum eminentem ex sifach, et preme ipsum ad profundum uentris.  
Then take a rod, and place it on the protruding area of the membrane, and press it to the depth of the abdomen.

Deinde sue duo loca eminentia super extremitatem radii ex sifach, et annecte cum sutura unum eorum cum altero: deinde extrahe extremitatem radii.  
Then sew the two protruding places over the end of the rod from the membrane, and connect one of them with the other using a suture: then withdraw the end of the rod.

Et non incidas alsifach omnino, neque tendas ouum, neque aliud, sicut feci te scire in curatione ramicis intestinalis.  
And do not cut the membrane entirely, nor extend the testicle, nor anything else, as I explained to you in the treatment of intestinal ruptures.

Deinde cura illud curatione uulnerum.  
Then treat it with wound care.

Cum ergo incidis fila, mundifica illud, et restaura uulnus, donec consolidetur.  
So when you cut the threads, clean it, and restore the wound until it is healed.

Sisach enim contrahitur, et non additur eminentia Rupturae.  
For the membrane contracts, and the protrusion of the rupture does not increase.

Et cauterium est melius in hoc loco: quoniam est propinquius ad salutem.  
And cautery is better in this location because it is closer to healing.

¶ De mollificatione cutis testiculorum.  
On the softening of the skin of the testicles.

Caput LXVIII.  
Chapter 68.

Multotiens mollificatur cutis testiculorum in quibusdam hominibus, propter quod mollificantur carnes quae sunt inter ea, et foedatur aspectus eius.  
Often the skin of the testicles becomes softened in some men, whereby the flesh between them is softened, and its appearance is disfigured.

Ergo necesse est ei qui rogatur in curatione eius, ut faciat iacere infirmum super dorsum suum, et incidat totam cutem quae mollificata est super cutem naturalem.  
Therefore, it is necessary for the one who is asked to treat it, to have the patient lie on his back, and to cut all the softened skin above the natural skin.

Deinde aggreget duo labia cum sutura: et si uis, sue in primis superfluitatem cutis mollificatae tribus suturis, aut quatuor, et firma suturam.  
Then join the two edges with suturing: and if you wish, sew the excess of the softened skin at first with three or four stitches, and secure the suture.

Deinde incide inter sututuras.  
Then cut between the sutures.

Deinde cura curatione reliquorum uulnerum, usquequo sanetur, et cadant fila.  
Then treat it with the care for other wounds, until it is healed and the threads fall out.

¶ De Castratione.  
On Castration.

Caput LXIX.  
Chapter 69.

Scias, quod Castratio in lege nostra excommunicata est: et propter illud liceret mihi, ut non rememorarer eius in libro meo isto: et non est necessaria rememoratio eius, nisi propter duos modos.  
Know that castration is condemned in our law: and because of that, it would be permissible for me to not mention it in this book of mine: and mentioning it is not necessary, except for two reasons.

Quorum unus est, ut sit illud in scientia medici quando interrogatur de ea: et ut sciat curationem eius cui accidit.  
One of which is so that it is in the knowledge of the physician when he is asked about it: and so that he knows the treatment of one to whom it happens.

Et modus alter est, quod nos multotiens indigemus castratione quorundam animalium, propter iuuamenta nostra per illud, sicut arietum, hyrcorum, et gattorum, et similium ex animalibus.  
And the other reason is that we often need to castrate certain animals for our benefit through it, such as rams, goats, cats, and similar animals.

Dico ergo, quod Castratio fit secundum duos modos.  
I say, therefore, that castration is done in two ways.

Aut per attritionem.  
Either by rubbing.

Aut per fissuram, et sectionem.  
Or by splitting and cutting.

In illa autem quae fit per attritionem, uia operationis est: quod nos faciamus sedere animal in aqua calida, donec mollificentur testiculi eius, et leniantur, et pendeant: deinde attere eos manu tua, donec resoluantur et non appareant sub tactu.  
In that which is done by rubbing, the method of operation is: that we make the animal sit in warm water, until its testicles are softened, relaxed, and hang down: then rub them with your hand, until they are dissolved and do not appear under touch.

In castratione autem per fissuram et sectionem, oportet ut teneas animal, et premas cutem testiculorum eius cum manu sinistra.  
In castration by splitting and cutting, however, it is necessary to restrain the animal, and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand.

Deinde liga suspensorium, et seca super omne ouum sectione una, donec quando procedunt duo oua: tunc incide ea postquam excoriaueris utrumque, et non dimittas super ea ex sifaket aliquid praeter sifac subtile, quod est super uasa.  
Then tie a suspensory band, and make one cut over each testicle until both testicles come out: then cut them after you have stripped each one, and leave nothing from the membrane except the thin layer, which is above the vessels.

Et iste modus castrationis est melior eo qui fit per attritonem: quoniam attritio fortasse relinquit aliquid ex testiculis, quare desiderat animal coitum.
And this method of castration is better than the one done by rubbing: because rubbing may perhaps leave something of the testicles, which causes the animal to desire mating.

Deinde cura uulnus, donec sanetur.
Then treat the wound until it is healed.

¶ De cura Hermafroditae duorum modorum.  
On the treatment of two types of hermaphroditism.

Caput LXX.  
Chapter 70.

Hermafrodita ex uiris est secundum duos modos.  
Hermaphroditism among males occurs in two forms.

Vnus eorum est, quia apparet in eo quod sequitur spacium, aut in cute testiculorum, in eo quod est inter duos testiculos, figura quasi uulua mulieris, in qua sunt pili: et quandoque currit urina ex eo quod est in cute testiculorum.  
One form appears as a space or in the skin of the testicles, between the two testicles, resembling the shape of a woman’s vulva, with hair present; and sometimes urine flows from the area in the skin of the testicles.

In mulieribus autem est species una, et est uulua mulieris super pectinem sicut testiculi uiri parui omnino, eminentes ad exteriora: quorum unus est sicut priapus uiri, et duo sicut duo testiculi.  
In women, there is one form where the vulva is located on the pubic area, resembling the small testicles of a male, slightly protruding outward: one part resembles a male penis, and two parts resemble two testicles.

Et curatio trium specierum, duarum ex uiris, et speciei unius ex mulieribus, est: quia oportet ut incidas carnes additas, donec effugiat impressio earum.  
The treatment for these three types—two forms in males and one form in females—is to cut away the excess flesh until its impression disappears.

Deinde cura eas curatione reliquorum uulnerum.  
Then, treat them with the usual wound care until healed.

In specie autem secunda uirorum, ex qua egreditur urina, quae est in cute testiculorum, non est operatio, neque est eius curatio omnino.  
For the second type in men, where urine flows from the skin of the testicles, there is no operation or treatment whatsoever.

¶ De incisione Tentiginis, et carnis eminentis in uuluis mulierum.  
On the excision of swelling and protruding flesh in the vulvas of women.

Caput LXXI.  
Chapter 71.

Tentigo fortasse additur super rem naturalem, donec foedatur et turpis fit aspectus eius: et quandoque magnificatur in quibusdam mulieribus adeo, donec expanditur sicut in uiris, et peruenit usque ad coitum.  
Swelling sometimes enlarges beyond the natural state, becoming disfigured and unsightly; in some women, it may grow to the extent that it expands like a male organ and becomes capable of sexual intercourse.

Oportet ergo ut teneas superfluitatem Tentiginis manu, aut cum uncino, et incidas: et non ultimes in incisione, praecipue in profundo radicis: ut non accidat fluxus sanguinis.  
Therefore, you should hold the excessive swelling with your hand or with a hook and cut it away; however, do not go too deep with the incision, especially at the base, to avoid bleeding.

Deinde cura ipsam curatione uulnerum, donec sanetur.  
Then treat the area with regular wound care until it heals.

Caro autem orta, est caro quae nascitur in orificio matricis, donec impleat ipsum: et fortasse egreditur ad exteriora secundum similitudinem caudae: et propter illud quidam primi nominant aegritudinem caudatam.  
Overgrown flesh may grow within the opening of the uterus until it fills the space; it may even protrude outward in a tail-like manner. Because of this, some early scholars called this ailment "caudate illness."

Oportet ergo ut incidamus eam sicut incidimus Tentiginem, et curemus eam, donec sanetur.  
Thus, we should excise it as we do for swelling, and treat it until it is healed.

¶ De cura Alratica, quae est uulua mulieris non perforata.  
On the treatment of Alratica, the condition of an imperforate vulva in women.

Caput LXXII.  
Chapter 72.

Alratica est, ut sit uulua mulieris non perforata, aut sit foramen paruum.  
Alratica is a condition where a woman’s vulva is either imperforate or has a very small opening.

Et est aut naturalis, aut accidentalis.  
It is either congenital or acquired.

Accidentalis est ex aegritudine quae praecessit: et ipsa quidem fit aut ex carne nata addita, aut sifach subtili, aut spisso: et fit aut in profundo matricis, aut in lateribus eius, aut in superiore ipsius, aut inferiori eius: et prohibet a coitu et impregnatione, et partu, et fortasse prohibet menstrua.  
The acquired form results from a previous ailment and may occur due to excess flesh growth or a membrane that is thin or thick; it may occur deep within the womb, on its sides, at its upper part, or lower part, and it obstructs intercourse, impregnation, and childbirth, and sometimes even menstruation.

Et cognitio illius fit per aspectum obstetricis, si opilatio est apparens propinqua.  
Diagnosis is made by a midwife’s examination if the obstruction is visible and close.

Si autem non est apparens, tunc quaere eam digitis tuis, aut cum radio.  
If it is not visible, then seek it out with your fingers or with a probe.

Si autem opilatio est ex sifach subtili, et est propinqua duobus labiis: tunc propera, et disrumpe ipsam.  
If the obstruction is due to a thin membrane and is close to the labia, then proceed quickly and rupture it.

Et est, ut ponas super duo labia puluillos.  
This is done by placing small cushions on both labia.

Deinde pone indices tuos duarum manuum simul, et mulier sit super dorsum suum expansis cruribus suis.  
Then place the index fingers of both hands together, while the woman lies on her back with her legs spread.

Deinde extende duo labia cum fortitudine, donec disrumpatur sifach subtile, et aperiatur opilatio.  
Then extend the two labia firmly until the thin membrane is ruptured and the obstruction is opened.

Deinde accipe lanam, et imbibe eam in oleo, et pone ipsam super locum: et coeat mulier omni die, ut non consolidetur locus uice alia.  
Next, take some wool, soak it in oil, and place it on the area; let the woman have intercourse daily to prevent the site from sealing again.

Si autem sifach est grossum, spissum: tunc oportet ut seces ipsum cum spatumili lato simili folio myrti.  
If the membrane is thick and dense, then you must cut it with a broad spatula shaped like a myrtle leaf.

Si autem opilatio est ex carne nata, tunc suspende eam cum uncinis, et incide eam: et sint tecum medicinae quae fluxum sedant sanguinis absque mordicatione, sicut acacia, et sanguis draconis, et thus aggregatum cum albugine oui.  
If the obstruction is due to excess flesh growth, suspend it with hooks and cut it away, and have on hand medicines that stop bleeding without causing irritation, such as acacia, dragon’s blood, and frankincense mixed with egg white.

Deinde administra cannulam ex plumbo amplam, ut non consolidetur uulnus uelociter, teneat eam diebus aliquot: et administra licinium ex lino sicco, deinde curetur reliqua curatione, donec sanetur.  
Then insert a broad lead tube to prevent the wound from closing too quickly, leaving it in place for a few days; apply a wick made from dry linen, then proceed with usual wound care until it heals.

Et quandoque nasciur in matrice natiuitas carnium aliarum: oportet ergo ut incidantur secundum hunc modum: dum non est apostema cancerosum apostemati enim canceroso quod est in matrice, non fiat contrarietas cum ferro omnino.  
Sometimes, new flesh growths arise in the womb. These must be excised as described here, provided there is no cancerous abscess; for a cancerous abscess in the womb, surgery with iron should not be performed at all.

¶ De cura hemorroidarum, Athehelil, et Bothor rubeae in uuluis mulierum.  
On the treatment of hemorrhoids, athehelil, and red bothor in the vulvae of women.

Caput LXXIII.  
Chapter 73.

Hemorroides quidem sunt apertio orificiorum uenarum, donec currit ex eis sanguis multus assidue.  
Hemorrhoids are indeed the opening of the orifices of veins, until much blood flows continually from them.

Cum ergo antiquantur hemorroides, fiunt thelil: et iam dixi in diuisione species earum, et signa ipsarum: et dicam hic quae ex eis recipiunt curationem, et quae non.  
When hemorrhoids persist, they become thelil; and I have already explained the types of these, and their signs; and I will say here which of them receive treatment, and which do not.

Dico ergo, quod hemorroides quae sunt in orificio matricis, et non apparent sensui: tunc non est ei curatio cum ferro.  
Therefore, I say that hemorrhoids that are in the orifice of the uterus and are not apparent to the senses: then they are not treated with a surgical instrument.

Quae autem ex eis sunt in orificio matricis super quas cadit sensus, sunt quae curantur.  
However, those that are in the orifice of the uterus and are perceived by touch are the ones that are treated.

Oportet ergo ut intromittas mulierem in domum frigidam.  
Therefore, it is necessary to place the woman in a cool room.

Deinde extende athehelil cum forficibus, aut cum panno aspero, et incide eas ex radicibus suis.  
Then stretch out the athehelil with scissors, or with a rough cloth, and cut them from their roots.

Deinde pulueriza super eas apud fluxum sanguinis ex uno puluerum incisiuorum absque mordificatione: sicut acacia, et sanguis draconis, et thus, et similia eis.  
Then sprinkle over them, where the blood flows, some powders of incision that do not cause stinging: such as acacia, dragon’s blood, frankincense, and similar substances.

Deinde impellat pedes eius ad parietem hora una.  
Then have her press her feet against the wall for one hour.

Postea depone eam in aquam frigidam.  
Afterwards, place her in cold water.

Quod si perseuerat fluxus sanguinis: tunc fac eam sedere in decoctione sumach, et corticum granatorum, et gallarum, et similium.  
If the blood flow persists, then make her sit in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate rind, galls, and similar ingredients.

Deinde accipe farinam hordei, et confice eam cum melle et aceto, et fac emplastrum cum eo super dorsum eius.  
Then take barley flour, mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster with it to place on her back.

Si ergo abscinditur sanguis cum eo, bonum est: et si non, fac adhaerere dorso uentosas, et mammillis, absque scarificatione.  
If the bleeding stops with this, it is good; if not, apply suction cups to her back and breasts, without cutting the skin.

Deinde accipe lanam, et submerge in succo tarathit, aut succo arnoglossae, aut succo ramorum alaulat, id est, aglanter, uino pontico, et fac adhaerere loeo.  
Then take wool, and soak it in the juice of tarathit, or the juice of plantain, or the juice of alaulat branches, that is, wild rose, with Pontic wine, and apply it to the area.

Cum ergo quiescit apostema, tunc cura locum cum unguentis, donec sanetur.  
When the swelling subsides, then treat the area with ointments until it heals.

Albarth uero rubeum est simile capitibus alhaasse, et est asperi aspectus.  
The red albarth is similar to the heads of alhaasse and has a rough appearance.

Oportet ergo ut incidas quod apparet ex eo, secundum quod dixi in thelil aequaliter: et cura ipsum, donec sanetur.  
Therefore, it is necessary to cut away what appears of it, as I have explained with the thelil, and treat it until it heals.

¶ De perforatione Exiturae quae accidit in matrice.  
On perforation of an ulcer occurring in the uterus.

Caput LXXIIII.  
Chapter 74.

Accidunt in matrice species multae apostematum, sicut cancer, et apostema lapideum, et ulcera, et adubelati, et alekilati, id est, herpes, aestiomemus, et fistulae, et hemorroides, et ragadiae, et thelil, et apostema calidum.  
Many types of swellings occur in the uterus, such as cancer, stone-like swellings, ulcers, adubelati, alekilati, that is, herpes, aestiomemus, fistulas, hemorrhoids, fissures, thelil, and hot swellings.

Et ego quidem iam dixi omnes has aegritudines et species earum, et signa ipsarum, et earum curationes in diuisione: necesse est ut dicam in hoc tractatu apostema calidum quod accidit in matrice, quando est ex apostematibus quae colligunt saniem, et uis scire qualiter fit eius apertio cum ferro.  
And indeed, I have already discussed all these afflictions, their types, their signs, and their treatments in the division; but it is necessary in this treatise to speak of the hot swelling that occurs in the uterus, when it is one of the swellings that collects pus, and you want to know how its opening is made with a surgical instrument.

Oportet ergo ut consideres.  
Therefore, it is necessary for you to observe.

Tunc si dolor apostematis in incaeptione sua est acutus cum percussione sua, et flamma, et febre: et uides ipsum rubere: si cadit super ipsum sensus, tunc non properes cum perforatione eius: et cura ipsum cum eo eo quod iuuat super maturationem, donec quando quiescat acuitas accidentium.  
Then, if the pain of the swelling is sharp at its beginning, with throbbing, heat, and fever, and you see it redden, and if it is sensitive to the touch, then do not rush to perforate it; treat it with what helps bring it to maturation until the sharpness of the symptoms subsides.

Tunc oportet ut facias sedere mulierem super sedem quae labeat duo sedilia, et reclinetur, uel appodietur super dorsum suum, et aggreget pedes suos ad partem inferiorem uentris: et sint coxae eius expansae, et ponat brachia sua sub genibus suis, et liget utraque ligamento conueniente ad illud.  
Then it is necessary to make the woman sit on a seat with two benches, and have her lean back or support herself on her back, bringing her feet toward the lower part of her abdomen; her hips should be spread, her arms placed under her knees, and each tied with a suitable binding for this.

Deinde sedeat obstetrix a latere dextro, et administra instrumentum quo aperitur orificium matricis.  
Then the midwife sits on her right side and uses the instrument that opens the orifice of the uterus.

Cuius forma uenit in eis quae sunt post.  
The form of this instrument is shown in the following illustrations.

Et oportet quando uis administrare hoc instrumentum, ut figas cum Radio profundum matricis mulieris: ut non sit illud quod ingreditur ex instrumento plus, quam profundum matricis, et laedat infirmam.  
And when you wish to use this instrument, you must affix the end of the probe in the depth of the woman’s uterus, so that what enters from the instrument does not go deeper than the depth of the uterus and harm the patient.

Si autem fuerit instrumentum magis quam profundum, tunc oportet ut ponas puluillos super tecturam profundi matricis: ut prohibeatur introitus instrumenti totius in profundum matricis: et oportet ut ponat uertiginem, quae currit in instrumento, ex latere superiore: et ut teneat instrumentum, et ut reuoluat minister uertiginem, donec aperiatur profundum matricis.  
If, however, the instrument is longer than necessary, you must place cushions over the covering of the depth of the uterus, to prevent the instrument from entering fully into the depth of the uterus; and the turning screw, which runs in the instrument, should be on the upper side, so the assistant holds the instrument and turns the screw until the depth of the uterus is opened.

Cum ergo apparet Exitura, et tangitur manu, et est lenis et mollis: tunc oportet ut seces ipsam apud caput suum cum spatumili lato.  
When the ulcer appears, can be touched by hand, and is smooth and soft, it is necessary to cut it at its head with a broad spatula.

Cum ergo euacuatur sanies, tunc oportet ut ponas in uulnus licinium submersum in oleo rosaceo: aut oleo uiridi, in quo sit quaedam stipticitas: et pone licinium, et extrahe sectionem in profundo matricis.  
When the pus is thus evacuated, you must place in the wound a linen cloth soaked in rose oil or green oil with a certain astringency; place the linen cloth and draw the section into the depth of the uterus.

Et pone exterius super matricem, et super pectinem lanam mundam submersam in aqua, in qua bullitae sunt maluae.  
Then place on the outside over the uterus and pubic area clean wool soaked in water in which mallows have been boiled.

Deinde curetur post duos dies cum unguento quod conuenit ad illud, donec sanetur.  
Then, after two days, treat it with an ointment suited to this purpose, until it heals.

Et quandoque abluitur matrix et uulnus, ita quod clisterizatur cum aqua et melle: deinde cum aqua in qua bullita est radix lilii, aut aristolochia longa: deinde redeat ad unguentum.  
And at times the uterus and the wound are washed, so that it is rinsed with water and honey; then with water in which lily root or long aristolochia has been boiled; then return to using the ointment.

Quod si uulnus absconditum fuerit interius in matrice, tunc oportet ut prohibearis ex curatione eius cum ferro, imo cura ipsum cum eo quod diximus in diuisione.  
If the wound is hidden within the uterus, then you must refrain from treating it with an instrument; rather, treat it with what we have discussed in the division.

¶ Doctrinae Obstetricum, qualiter medicentur embriones uiui, secundum figuram non naturalem egressi.  
Teachings for Midwives, on how to treat live embryos, when they emerge in an unnatural position.

Caput Lxxu.  
Chapter 75.

Necesse est Obstetrici, ut cognoscat in primis figuram partus naturalis.  
It is necessary for the midwife first to know the form of natural birth.

Ex signis ergo eius est, quod quando uides mulierem comprimi ad inferiora, et desiderat odorare aerem, et alleuiatur super eam quod super ipsam est de partu, et festinat exitus embrionis: tunc scias quod iste partus est secundum figuram naturalem, et est exitus eius super caput suum, et secundina cum eo: aut suspensa, uel pendens ex umbilico.  
Among the signs of this is that when you see the woman bearing down, and she desires to smell fresh air, and the pressure from labor lessens over her, and the embryo's exit hastens, then you know that this birth is according to the natural form, and its exit is head-first with the afterbirth, either attached or hanging from the umbilical cord.

Cum ergo uides haec signa, tunc oportet ut comprimatur uenter eius, ut descendat embrio uelociter.  
When you see these signs, it is then necessary to press on her abdomen so that the embryo descends quickly.

Nam quando descendit super caput suum, descendit secundina cum eo, et mundatur ex illis superfluitatibus mundificatione bona.  
For when it descends head-first, the afterbirth descends with it, and it is cleansed of these impurities with good purification.

Qui autem est praeter hunc partum, est innaturalis, illaudabilis.  
But any other birth than this is unnatural and unfavorable.

Quoniam quandoque egreditur foetus super pedes suos, et egreditur corpus eius ante caput ipsius, et pedes eius, et manus eius una, aut pes eius unus: aut egreditur caput eius et manus eius: aut egreditur uentrinus: et fortasse conuertitur super collum suum, et similia ex figuris illaudabilibus.  
For sometimes the fetus emerges feet-first, or its body exits before its head, with one foot or hand, or one foot alone; or its head and hand emerge; or its abdomen appears; and perhaps it turns on its neck, and other such unfavorable presentations.

Necesse est ergo Obstetrici, ut sit prudens, subtilis in istis rebus omnibus, et caueat sibi ab errore et decaeptione: et ego sum ostendens omnem figuram ex eis, et qualiter est ingenium in ea, et significetur per illud, et stetur super ipsum.  
Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise, precise in all these matters, and cautious of error and deception; and I am showing every one of these forms and how to manage each, and it shall be explained and demonstrated.

Quando egreditur foetus super caput suum egressione sua naturali, et uehemens fit illud super mulierem, et difficilis fit ei partus, et uides uirtutem eius iam debilitatam: tunc fac eam sedere super sedem, aut mulieres teneant eam: et uapora uuluam eius cum foenugraeco decocto, et cum oleis humidis.  
When the fetus emerges head-first in its natural exit, and this becomes intense for the woman, and the birth becomes difficult for her, and you see her strength already weakened: then have her sit on a seat, or have other women hold her, and steam her vulva with a fenugreek decoction and moist oils.

Deinde intromittat Obstetrix inter digitos suos Spatumile paruum, et findat cum eo secundinam, et secet eam ungue suo, donec currat quod est in ea ex humiditate: et preme uentrem mulieris, donec descendat foetus.  
Then let the midwife insert between her fingers a small spatula and split the afterbirth with it, cutting it with her fingernail until the moisture contained within flows out; and press the woman's abdomen until the fetus descends.

Si autem non descendit, tunc oportet ut clisterizetur mulier ex mucillagine foenugraeci, cum oleo sisamino.  
If it does not descend, then the woman must be given an enema of fenugreek mucilage with sesame oil.

Deinde praecipe ei post clistere, ut comprimatur: et fac eam sternutare cum condisi, et tene os eius et nasum ipsius hora una.  
Then instruct her after the enema to bear down; and make her sneeze with condiments, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour.

Foetus enim egredietur statim.  
The fetus will then emerge immediately.

Quod si egrediantur duae manus foetus in primis, iunc oportet ut reducas eas cum facilitate paulatim.  
But if the two hands of the fetus emerge first, then it is necessary to gently and gradually push them back.

Si autem non obedit in introitu, tunc pone mulierem super sedem, et eleua pedes eius sursum: deinde concute sedem super terram: et mulier teneatur, ut non cadat apud concussionem.  
If it does not go back easily, then place the woman on a seat and lift her feet upwards; then shake the seat over the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall during the shaking.

Si ergo non egrediuntur manus, et moritur foetus: tunc incide eas, et extrahe residuum foetus: et liga manum eius cum panno, et extrahe ipsum cum aequalitate: nam ipse egredietur.  
If, however, the hands do not come out and the fetus dies, then cut them off and extract the rest of the fetus; bind its hand with cloth and draw it out steadily, and it will emerge.

### Exitus Embrionis Super Pedes Suos
_When the fetus emerges feet-first_

Quando egreditur foetus super pedes suos, tunc oportet ut impellat eos sursum: deinde conuertat foetum paulatim: postea aequet ipsum.  
When the fetus emerges feet-first, it is necessary to push the feet upward, then gradually turn the fetus, and then adjust its position.

Deinde accipiat unum pedum eius, et extendat eum paulatim.  
Then take one of its feet and extend it gradually.

Cum ergo egrediuntur usque ad coxas, tunc praecipe ei, ut comprimatur, et fac eam sternutare cum condisi: egredietur enim, si Deus uoluerit.  
When the fetus emerges up to the hips, instruct the woman to bear down, and make her sneeze with a condiment; then the fetus will emerge, God willing.

Et si non egreditur cum eo quod narrauimus, tunc reduc foetum paulatim, donec ponas eum secundum figuram naturalem.  
If the fetus does not emerge with this approach, then gradually push it back until it is in the natural position.

Nam ipse egredietur tunc egressu facili.  
Then it will emerge easily.

Quod si prohibeatur cum eo toto quod narrauimus: tunc accipe ex mucillagine alteae, et oleo sisamino, et gummi soluto: et percute totum in mortario percussione bona: deinde line cum eo uuluam mulieris, et inferius uentris eius.  
But if it is still prevented from emerging with all that we have described, then take marshmallow mucilage, sesame oil, and dissolved gum; pound everything thoroughly in a mortar, then apply it to the woman’s vulva and lower abdomen.

Deinde fac eam sedere in aqua tepida, donec consequatur hypocundria.  
Next, have her sit in warm water until her lower abdomen relaxes.

Cum ergo uides quod iam calefacta sunt inferiora eius, tunc fac ei sief de myrrha: et suppone ipsum.  
When you see that her lower parts are now warmed, then prepare a suppository of myrrh and place it.

Quando ergo tenet sief hora una, tunc fac eam sedere super sedem.  
When she has held the suppository for an hour, then have her sit on a seat.

Deinde fac eam sternutare: et stringe ipsius os et nasum: et preme inferiorem partem uentris compressione facili.  
Next, make her sneeze, and gently press her mouth and nose, and apply gentle pressure on her lower abdomen.

Nam foetus egredietur statim.  
The fetus will then emerge immediately.

### Exitus Foetus Super Genua et Manus
_When the fetus emerges on its knees and hands_

Quando egreditur secundum hanc formam, tunc ingeniet in intromittendo manus suas paulatim.  
When the fetus emerges in this way, she must carefully insert her hands gradually.

Deinde resupinetur mulier super collum suum, et pendeant pedes eius ad inferiora: et ipsa sit iacens super lectum, et complicet manus suas.  
Then the woman should be laid back on her neck, with her legs hanging down, lying on the bed with her hands folded.

Deinde preme supra uentrem eius paulatim.  
Then gently press on her abdomen.

Deinde extrahe quod est sub pedibus eius ex puluinaribus, donec sit praeparata in inferiori parte.  
Then remove what is beneath her feet from the cushions, so that she is prepared at the lower part.

Quod si non egreditur foetus, tunc accipe pedes eius, et moue eos motu uehementi.  
If the fetus does not emerge, take its feet and shake them with firm motion.

Deinde preme quod est supra hypocundria paulatim, donec ascendat foetus ad superiora.  
Next, press gradually above the lower abdomen until the fetus moves upward.

Deinde intromittat manus suas, et aequet foetum paulatim: et praecipe mulieri, ut comprimatur, donec egrediatur foetus.  
Then insert her hands, gradually aligning the fetus, and instruct the woman to bear down until the fetus emerges.

### Exitus Foetus Latitudinaliter Pendens Ex Manibus
_When the fetus is hanging laterally by its arms_

Ingenietur in reductione manus eius.  
Carefully attempt to reposition its hand.

Si autem non potest reducere eam, tunc eleua mulierem, et fac eam ambulare.  
If this is not possible, then lift the woman and have her walk.

Si uero ambulare non potest, tunc fac eam iacere super lectum: et concute crura eius concussione uehementi.  
If she cannot walk, then lay her on the bed and shake her legs firmly.

Deinde administra linimentum quod praeparasti ex mucillaginibus.  
Next, apply the liniment prepared from mucilage.

Quod si accipit eam partus, tunc fac eam sedere super sedem.  
If labor seizes her, then have her sit on a seat.

Deinde stude in reductione manus, et aequa foetum secundum figuram naturalem: et fac sternutare mulierem, et praecipe ei, ut comprimat se, donec egrediatur.  
Then work on repositioning its hand and align the fetus in the natural position, and make the woman sneeze, instructing her to bear down until the fetus emerges.

### Exitus Foetus Super Collum Suum, Expansis Manibus, et Est Facies Eius ad Dorsum Matris Suae
_When the fetus emerges head-down, with arms extended, and its face toward the mother's back_

Oportet ut teneat Obstetrix manum foetus, deinde reuoluat eum paulatim, et aequet eum cum facilitate.  
The midwife must hold the fetus’s hand, then turn it gently and adjust it with ease.

Cum ergo aequatur, tunc pone super uuluam eius quod narrauimus ex oleo et mucillaginibus.  
When it is properly aligned, then apply the mixture of oil and mucilage on her vulva as we described.

Deinde praecipe ei, ut moueatur paulatim.  
Then instruct her to move gradually.

Cum ergo feceris illud, tunc fac eam sedere super sedem, et praecipe ei ut inclinetur ad latus dextrum.  
When you have done this, have her sit on a seat and instruct her to lean to her right side.

Deinde praecipe ei, ut comprimatur: et fac eam sternutare cum condisi.  
Then instruct her to bear down and make her sneeze with condiments.

### Exitus Foetus Praeparati Super Latus
_When the fetus is positioned sideways_

Quando descendit ad orificium matricis secundum hunc modum cum secundina, tunc scinde secundinam cum ungue tuo, donec euacuetur ex humiditate.  
When the fetus descends to the mouth of the uterus in this manner with the afterbirth, then cut the afterbirth with your fingernail until the moisture is released.

Si ergo suspenditur super faciem foetus, et collum eius, tunc incide eam ex umbilico: ut non retineatur, et moriatur.  
If it then hangs over the face and neck of the fetus, cut it from the umbilical cord, so it does not hold it back and cause death.

Deinde impelle foetum ad interiora, donec ponas eum secundum quod oportet: et praecipe mulieri, ut comprimat se aliquotiens: ipse enim egredietur exitu leui.  
Then push the fetus back inward until it is in the appropriate position, and instruct the woman to bear down several times; then it will emerge with ease.

¶ Exitus Geminorum, aut foetuum multorum.  
The exit of twins, or of many fetuses.

Scias, quod Gemini multotiens nascuntur: et quandoque nascuntur tres, et quatuor.  
Know that twins are often born, and sometimes three or four are born.

Verumtamen illud extraneum est, et raro contingit.  
However, that is unusual and rarely happens.

Quinque uero est res extra naturam, et non uiuunt penitus: et continet eos, quamuis multiplicentur, secundina una: et separantur per sifach, distinguens inter eos ligatum in umbilico cuiusque eorum.  
But five is something unnatural, and they do not survive at all; even if they are multiple, they are contained in one membrane, and are separated by a membrane, distinguishing between them a ligament in each of their umbilici.

Et quandoque egrediuntur sicut egreditur foetus unus exitu naturali, facili: et egrediuntur exitu illaudabili, sicut narrauimus.  
And sometimes they emerge as one fetus does, with a natural, easy exit; and they emerge with a difficult exit, as we have described.

Quod si difficiles fuerint quidam eorum apud partum, et perueniunt ad illud quod diximus ex figuris innaturalibus, tunc cura eos sicut narrauimus: et sit ob stetrix subtilis, et faciat quod facit cum facilitate et tarditate, et ingenietur secundum omnem figuram cum eo quod praeparatur ei ex ingenio ducente ad salutem.  
But if any of them are difficult at birth, and they come to the situation we mentioned with unnatural positions, then care for them as we have described, and let the midwife be skillful, and let her act with ease and patience, and use her ingenuity in every position with what is prepared for her, guided toward safety.

¶ Rememoratio eius quod formatur in matrice ex embrionibus, et abortiuntur.  
Recollection of what is formed in the womb from embryos, and is aborted.

Quandoque formatur in matrice unus, et duo, et tres, et quatuor, et quinque, et sex, et septem, et plures decem: et iam uerificatum est apud me, quod mulier abortiendo emisit septem, et alia quindecim, omnes formatos.  
Sometimes one is formed in the womb, or two, or three, or four, or five, or six, or seven, or more, up to ten; and it has been verified by me that a woman in aborting expelled seven, and another fifteen, all fully formed.

Quod factum est mensuratione gloriosi sapientis.  
Which was accomplished by the measurement of a glorious sage.

Hoc ergo totum oportet ut sit in scientia Obstetricis.  
Therefore, all this must be in the knowledge of the midwife.

Fortasse enim perueniet ad eam simile illius: opponat ergo ei cum illo quod oportet.  
For perhaps something similar to that may come to her; let her, therefore, apply to it whatever is necessary.

¶ De extractione foetus mortui.  
On the extraction of a dead fetus.

Caput LXXVI.  
Chapter 76.

Quando curas foetum mortuum cum eo quod dixi in diuisione ex medicatione, et non egreditur, et cogeris uti operatione cum manu, tunc oportet ut consideres.  
When you treat a dead fetus with what I have discussed in the section on medication, and it does not emerge, and you are forced to use manual intervention, then you must consider.

Si ergo mulier est sanae uirtutis, et non est cum aliquo ex accidentibus, ex quibus timetur super eam perditio: tunc oportet ut resupinetur mulier super lectum, super dorsum suum, et sit caput eius inclinatum inferius, et crura eius eleuata: et ministra teneat eam a duabus partibus, aut ligetur ad lectum, ut non extrahatur corpus eius apud extractionem foetus.  
If the woman is of sound strength and does not have any conditions that would threaten her life, then the woman should be laid on her back on a bed, with her head inclined downward and her legs elevated; an assistant should hold her from both sides, or she should be bound to the bed, so that her body is not pulled during the fetus's extraction.

Deinde humecta os matricis ex oleis humidis cum mucillagine alteae, et foenugraeci, et seminis lini.  
Then moisten the mouth of the uterus with softening oils made with the mucilage of mallow, fenugreek, and flaxseed.

Deinde inungat Obstetrix manum suam cum istis oleis et mucillaginibus: deinde intromittat eam in matricem cum facilitate.  
Then the midwife should anoint her hand with these oils and mucilages, and then insert it into the uterus gently.

Deinde quaerat cum ea locum in quo figat uncinos ex foetu, et loca conuenientia ad illud.  
Then she should look with her hand for a place where she can secure hooks into the fetus, and find suitable locations for this.

Considera ergo tunc, si foetus est praeparatus ut descendat super caput suum: tunc fige uncinos in oculos eius, aut in collo eius, aut in ore eius, aut in palato ipsius, aut sub barba eius, aut in furcula ipsius, aut in locis propinquis costis, et sub hypocundriis.  
Therefore, if the fetus is positioned to descend head first, then place the hooks in its eyes, or its neck, or its mouth, or its palate, or under its chin, or its breastbone, or in locations near the ribs and under the hypochondria.

Si autem descensus est super pedes eius, tunc in pectine, et costis eius mediis.  
If, however, it descends feet first, then in its groin and middle ribs.

Et oportet, ut teneat uncinum cum manu dextra: et ponat curuitatem eius in eo quod est inter digitos sinistrae manus: et intromittat cum manu cum facilitate, et figat uncinum in aliquo illorum locorum quae diximus, donec perueniat ad rem uacuam.  
She should hold the hook with her right hand and place its curve between the fingers of her left hand; then insert it with ease and secure the hook in one of those locations mentioned, until she reaches an empty space.

Deinde figat in oppositione eius uncinum alium, aut tertium, si indiges: ut sit contractio aequalis, et non declinet ad partem.  
Then she should fix another hook opposite it, or a third if needed, so that the pull is even and does not lean to one side.

Deinde extendatur extensione aequali, et non sit extensio secundum rectitudinem tantum, imo moueatur ad omnem partem, ut alleuietur exitus eius: sicut fit cum dente apud eradicationem eius.  
Then pull with equal force, not only in a straight line, but move it in all directions, to ease its exit, as is done with a tooth during extraction.

Et oportet in eo quod est inter illud, ut mollificetur extensio.  
And it is necessary that, in between these actions, the extension is softened.

Quod si retineatur ex eo pars, tunc oportet ut inungat Obstetrix quosdam digitos cum oleo, et intromittat eos ex parte, ut reuoluat cum eis quod retinetur.  
If a part is held back, then the midwife should anoint some of her fingers with oil and insert them from the side, to rotate what is being held.

Si ergo egreditur pars foetus, tunc permutentur uncini ad locum alium qui sit altior: fac hoc donec egrediatur foetus totus.  
If a part of the fetus emerges, then shift the hooks to a higher location; do this until the entire fetus exits.

Si ergo egreditur manus ante alia, et non est possibile reducere eam, propter coartationem eius: tunc oportet, ut inuoluatur super eam pannus.  
If a hand emerges before the others, and it is impossible to push it back due to its restriction, then it should be wrapped in a cloth.

Deinde extrahe eam donec quando egreditur tota, incide eam aut in iunctura plantae, aut in cubito: et ita oportet ut facias in manu altera, et in duobus pedibus.  
Then pull it until it fully exits, and cut it either at the wrist or elbow; do likewise with the other hand and both feet.

Si autem caput foetus est magnum, aut accidit ei coartatio in exitu, aut est in capite eius aqua aggregata: tunc oportet ut intromittat inter digitos Spatumile spinosum, et findat cum eo caput, et extrahat aquam: aut disrumpat ipsum cum instrumento quod nominatur Almisdac: cuius forma uenit cum formis reliquorum instrumentorum in capitulo quod est post hoc.  
If, however, the fetus's head is large, or it is restricted in the exit, or there is fluid accumulated in its head, then it is necessary to insert between the fingers a thorny spatumile, and split the head with it to extract the fluid, or rupture it with an instrument called an Almisdac, the form of which appears with the other instrument forms in the chapter after this one.

Similiter faciat si foetus est magni capitis natura, tunc oportet ut seces algengematu: aut extrahas ipsum cum misdach, sicut diximus.  
Similarly, if the fetus has a naturally large head, then it is necessary to cut it with the algengematu or extract it with the misdach, as we have described.

Deinde attrahas ossa cum forcipibus.  
Then pull out the bones with forceps.

Quod si egrediatur caput, et coartetur apud furculam: tunc findatur, donec effundatur humiditas quae est in pectore.  
If the head emerges but becomes restricted at the breastbone, then it should be split until the moisture in the chest is released.

Si autem non complicatur, neque obedit ad exitum: tunc incide caput frustatim, secundum quod possibile est tibi.  
If it does not fold or permit exit, then cut the head into pieces as much as is possible for you.

Quod si inferius uentris est apostematum, aut est in eo hydropisis: tunc oportet ut perfores ipsum, donec currat humiditas ex eo.  
If there is an abscess in the lower abdomen, or if there is dropsy in it, then it is necessary to pierce it until the fluid flows out.

Si uero foetus est super pedes suos, tunc attractio eius est facilis, et directio eius ad os matricis est leuis.  
If the fetus is on its feet, then its extraction is easy, and its direction toward the mouth of the uterus is smooth.

Si autem coartatur apud uentrem, aut pectus: tunc oportet ut extrahas ipsum cum panno quem inuoluisti super manum tuam: et findat uentrem, aut pectus, donec currat quod est in eis.  
If it becomes restricted at the abdomen or chest, then it is necessary to extract it with a cloth wrapped around your hand, and split the abdomen or chest until the contents flow out.

Si autem auferuntur reliqua membra, et redit caput: tunc intromittat Obstetrix manum sinistram.  
If the other limbs have been removed and the head remains, then the midwife should insert her left hand.

Si ergo os matricis est apertum, tunc intromittat manum in profundum matricis, et quaerat cum ea caput, et attrahat ipsum cum digitis usque ad os matricis: deinde intromittat in eo uncinum unum, aut uncinos duos, et attrahat ipsum cum eo.  
If the mouth of the uterus is open, then she should insert her hand deep into the uterus, search for the head with it, and draw it toward the mouth of the uterus with her fingers; then insert one hook or two into it and pull it out with them.

Quod si os matricis coartatur, propter apostema calidum quod accidit ei: tunc non oportet ut laboretur super ipsum, imo oportet tunc administrare effusionem rerum humidarum, pinguium: et administra emplastra: et sedeat in aquis quae mollificant et humectant.  
If the mouth of the uterus is restricted due to a warm abscess that has occurred, then it is not necessary to work on it; rather, it is necessary to apply moist, fatty substances, apply poultices, and have her sit in waters that soften and moisten.

Quod si foetus est super latus suum, tunc possibile est ut aequetur: tunc administretur quod diximus in foetu uiuo.  
If the fetus is on its side, then it is possible to straighten it; then apply the same treatment that we discussed for a live fetus.

Quod si non est possibile illud, tunc incidatur frustatim, et extrahatur.  
If that is not possible, then it should be cut into pieces and extracted.

Et oportet ut non dimittas aliquid ex secundina intus omnino.  
And it is necessary not to leave any part of the afterbirth inside at all.

Cum ergo compleueris operationem tuam, tunc administra quod diximus in apostematibus calidis quae accidunt in matricibus.  
When you have completed your operation, then administer what we mentioned regarding warm abscesses that occur in the uterus.

Quod si accidat fluxus sanguinis, tunc descendat in aquis stipticis, et administra reliquam curationem.  
If bleeding occurs, then let her sit in astringent waters and administer the remaining treatment.

Et ego quidem iam uidi mulierem, in cuius uentre mortuus erat foetus: deinde impregnata est super ipsum uice alia, postea mortuus est foetus alius etiam.  
I myself have seen a woman in whose womb a fetus had died; she then became pregnant again over it, and afterward that fetus also died.

Accidit ergo ei post tempus longum apostema in umbilico suo, et inflatum est, donec apertum est: et coepit emittere pus.  
After a long time, an abscess developed in her navel, and it swelled until it opened and began to discharge pus.

Vocatus sum ergo ad curationem eius, et medicatus sum ei tempore longo: et non consolidatum est uulnus.  
I was called to treat her, and I treated her for a long time, but the wound did not heal.

Posui ergo super ipsum ex quibusdam emplastris fortis attractionis: et exiuit ex loco os.  
So I applied to it some poultices with strong drawing power, and a bone came out of the place.

Deinde praeterierunt ei dies aliquot, et exiuit os aliud.  
Then, after a few days, another bone emerged.

Miratus sum ergo inde, cum in uentre non sit os.  
I was amazed at this, since there are no bones in the womb.

Cogitaui ergo, quia erant ex ossibus foetus mortui.  
So I thought that they were bones of the dead fetus.

Inquisiui ergo uulnus, et extraxi ossa multa, muliere existente in melioribus dispositionibus suis: et iam uixit taliter tempore longo, et mittit ex loco pus parum.  
I therefore explored the wound and extracted many bones, the woman being in better health, and she continued to live in this condition for a long time, discharging a small amount of pus from the place.

Et ego non firmaui hic hoc extraneum, nisi quoniam in eo est scientia, et adiutorium ad illud, quod administrat medicus artifex cum manu ex curatione.  
I record this unusual case here only because it contains knowledge and assistance for what the skillful physician accomplishes by hand in treatment.

¶ De formis Instrumentorum necessariorum in extractione foetus.  
On the forms of instruments necessary for the extraction of the fetus.  

Caput LXXVII.  
Chapter 77.  

Hic inferius est forma Strictorii, quo aequantur libri, cui aequaliter sunt duae uertigines in duabus extremitatibus duorum lignorum.  
Below is the form of the press, by which books are aligned, having two equal pivots at the two ends of two wooden pieces.  

Verumtamen haec Vertigo oportet ut sit subtilior strictorio: et ut fiat, aut ex ebano, aut ex ligno bussi.  
However, this pivot should be finer than the press and should be made either of ebony or boxwood.  

Et sit latitudo omnis ligni quasi duo digiti: et margo cuiusque amborum est quasi digitus unus, et longitudo cuiusque eorum est palmus et medietas: et in medio duorum lignorum sunt duo additamenta ex genere eiusdem ligni, quae iam firmata sunt in utrisque, quorum longitudo est medietas palmi et plus parum: et latitudo utriusque est quasi duo digiti, aut plus parum.  
The width of each piece of wood should be about two fingers, with each side margin being about one finger, and the length of each piece is a palm and a half. In the middle of the two wooden pieces are two additional parts made of the same kind of wood, already fixed to each side, with a length of half a palm and slightly more, and the width of each is about two fingers, or a little more.  

Et ista duo additamenta intromittuntur in os matricis, ut aperiatur cum eis quando tu reuoluis duas Vertigines.  
These two additional parts are inserted into the mouth of the womb, to open it when you turn the two pivots.  

Forma Vertiginis qua aperitur matrix.  
The form of the pivot with which the womb is opened.  

Forma alia ad simile illius, subtilior, et leuior.  
Another form similar to it, finer and lighter.  

Fiat ex ligno ebani, aut bussi, secundum similitudinem forcipum.  
It should be made from ebony or boxwood, in the likeness of forceps.  

Verumtamen in extremitate eius sint duo additamenta, sicut uides hic supra: et longitudo omnis additamenti ex eis est quasi palmus: et latitudo utriusque est, duo digiti.  
However, at its end should be two additional parts, as you see above; the length of each part is about a palm, and the width of each is two fingers.  

Cum ergo uis aperire matricem cum eo, tunc fac sedere mulierem super lectum, pendentibus pedibus eius, aperto quod est inter crura eius.  
Therefore, when you wish to open the womb with it, have the woman sit on a bed with her feet hanging down and the area between her legs exposed.  

Deinde intromitte ista duo additamenta coniuncta in matricem: et tu es tenens extremitatem instrumenti inferius inter coxas eius.  
Then insert the two joined additional parts into the womb, holding the instrument's end below between her thighs.  

Deinde aperi manum tuam cum instrumento, sicut facis cum forficibus, aequaliter secundum quantitatem quam uis ex apertione oris matricis, donec faciat Obstetrix quod uult.  
Then open your hand with the instrument, as you would with scissors, according to the amount you wish to open the mouth of the womb, until the midwife achieves what she wants.  

Forma Vertiginis alterius quam dixerunt antiqui Forma Impellentis quo impellitur foetus.  
The form of another pivot which the ancients called the form of the pusher, with which the fetus is pushed.  

Forma Almisdac, qua conteritur caput magnum: et assimilatur forcipi, cui sunt dentes in extremitate, sicut uides.  
The form of the Almisdac, with which a large head is crushed; it resembles forceps with teeth at the end, as you see.  

Et quandoque fit oblungum, sicut forcipes secundum hanc formam, sicut uides, cui sunt dentes sicut dentes serrae, quo inciditur et conteritur.  
And it is sometimes made elongated, like forceps of this form, as you see, with teeth like those of a saw, with which it cuts and crushes.  

Forma Almisdac quo conteritur caput paruum.  
The form of the Almisdac with which a small head is crushed.  

Forma Vncini habentis spinam unam.  
The form of the hook with one spine.  

Forma Vncini habentis spinas duas.  
The form of the hook with two spines.  

Forma forcipis cui sunt dentes serrae, cum quo conteritur caput foetus.  
The form of forceps with serrated teeth, with which the head of the fetus is crushed.  

Forma Spatumilis habentis duas extremitates ad abscindendum caput.  
The form of the Spatumilis with two ends for cutting off the head.  

Forma duorum Spatumilium etiam latorum.  
The form of two wide Spatumilia.  

Ista instrumenta omnia exercentur, et quanto plus multiplicantur species eorum, et praeparata sunt apud artificem, est uelocior ad operationem suam, et altior apud homines, propter quantitatem suam.  
All these instruments are used, and the more their types are multiplied and prepared by the craftsman, the quicker they are for the operation and more esteemed by people, due to their quantity.  

Non ergo despicies ex eis instrumentum, quin sit apud te praeparatum.  
Therefore, do not disregard any of these instruments; have them prepared with you.  

Inexcusabilis est enim necessitas eorum.  
For their necessity is undeniable.  

¶ De extractione Secundinae.  
On the extraction of the afterbirth.  

Caput LXXVIII.  
Chapter 78.  

Quando retinetur Secundina apud partum, tunc oportet ut praecipias infirmae, ut retineat anhelitum suum.  
When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, then you should instruct the patient to hold her breath.  

Deinde fac eam sternutare cum condisi: et stringe manum tuam super os eius, et nares ipsius.  
Then make her sneeze with a condiment, and press your hand over her mouth and nose.  

Si ergo egreditur per hoc, bonum est.  
If it comes out as a result, it is good.  

Si non: tunc accipe ollam, et perfora in coopertorio foramen: et pone in ea herbas aperientes os matricis, sicut calamentum, rutam, et anetum, et camomillam, et sseham, et cassiam ligneam, et centauream: accipe omnes istas herbas, aut quasdam earum, et submerge eas cum aqua, et pone eas super ignem.  
If not, then take a pot and perforate a hole in the cover, and place in it herbs that open the mouth of the womb, like calamint, rue, dill, chamomile, sseha, cinnamon, and centaury; take all these herbs, or some of them, and submerge them in water, and place them on the fire.  

Deinde pone embulam arundinis super foramen coopertorii ollae, et extremitatem aliam in os matricis: et teneat eam donec perueniat uapor ad concauitatem matricis.  
Then place a reed tube over the hole in the cover of the pot, and place the other end in the mouth of the womb; let her hold it until the vapor reaches the cavity of the womb.  

Deinde fac eam sternutare, sicut diximus.  
Then make her sneeze, as we have said.  

Secundina enim egredietur cum facilitate.  
For the afterbirth will come out with ease.  

Si autem remaneat post hanc curationem, et non egrediatur: tunc praecipe Obstetrici, ut submergat manum suam in oleo sisamino, aut mucillagine alteae.  
If it remains after this treatment and does not come out, then instruct the midwife to dip her hand in sesame oil or marshmallow mucilage.  

Deinde intromittat in uuluam, et quaerat cum ea Secundinam.  
Then she should insert her hand into the vulva and search for the afterbirth with it.

Cum ergo inuenerit eam, tunc accipiat eam, et extendat ipsam paulatim.  
When she finds it, then she should take hold of it and gently stretch it out little by little.  

Si autem fuerit annexa in profundo matricis, tunc intromittat manum, secundum quod narrauimus, donec quando inuenerit Secundinam, et extrahat eam paulatim secundum rectitudinem, ut non cadat matrix apud attractionem uehementem: imo oportet, ut permutetur cum facilitate ad latera dextra et sinistra: deinde addatur in quantitatem attractionis.  
But if it is attached deep within the womb, she should insert her hand, as we have described, until she finds the afterbirth, and pull it out gradually in a straight line, so the womb does not fall due to forceful traction; rather, it should be moved gently to the right and left sides, then more traction may be applied as needed.  

Ipsa enim obedit tunc, et seruatur, et euadit ab adhaerentia.  
Then it yields, is freed, and escapes from its adherence.  

Quod si os matricis est coartatum, sicut nos iam narrauimus: cura eam cum sternutatione, et ex medicatione ollae cum herbis.  
If the mouth of the womb is constricted, as we have already described, treat her with sneezing and the medication from the pot with herbs.  

Si autem non egreditur cum omnibus quae narrauimus, tunc caue ne fatigeris super eam in iteratione extractionis.  
If it does not come out with everything we have described, then be careful not to exhaust her with repeated extractions.  

Verum oportet, ut quod egreditur ad os matricis ex ea, liges ad coxam mulieris.  
Instead, it is proper to tie what comes out at the mouth of the womb to the woman's hip.  

Deinde clisteriza eam cum unguento tetrapharmacon.  
Then administer a clyster with tetrapharmacon ointment.  

Ipsum enim putrefaciet eam post dies, et dissoluetur, et egredietur.  
For this will cause it to decay over days, dissolve, and come out.  

Verumtamen quando putrefit, eleuatur ex ea odor malus ad stomachum et caput, et laedit illud infirmam.  
However, when it decays, a foul odor will rise from it to her stomach and head, harming the patient.  

Oportet ergo ut administrentur suffumigationes conuenientes ad illud.  
Therefore, suitable fumigations should be administered for this.  

Quidam autem antiquorum iam experti sunt suffumigationem nasturtii, et ficuum siccarum.  
Some of the ancients have tried fumigations with watercress and dried figs.  

Forma instrumenti quo suffumigatur mulier apud retentionem Secundinae et menstruorum.  
The form of the instrument with which a woman is fumigated for retention of the afterbirth and menstruation.  

Fiat ex uitro simile alcama, aut ex zere: et ponatur extremitas ampla super ignem: et suffumigatio sit posita super prunas: teneat eam, donec consumatur illa suffumigatio: et itera aliam.  
It should be made of glass similar to alcama, or from bronze; place the wide end over the fire, and the fumigation is placed on the embers; she should hold it until the fumigation is consumed, and repeat another.  

¶ De curatione Ani non perforati.  
On the treatment of an imperforate anus.  

Caput LXXIX.  
Chapter 79.  

Nascuntur multi puerorum, et Ani eorum sunt non perforati, quos iam opilauit sifac subtile.  
Many children are born with their anuses not perforated, which a delicate membrane has obstructed.  

Oportet ergo, ut obstetrix perforet illud sifac digito suo: et si non, perforet ipsum cum Spatumili acuto: et caueat lacertum, ne tangat eum.  
Therefore, the midwife should perforate that membrane with her finger; if not, she should perforate it with a sharp Spatumili and be careful not to touch the muscle.  

Deinde pone super ipsum lanam infusam in uino et oleo.  
Then place wool soaked in wine and oil over it.  

Deinde cura ipsum cum ungentis, donec sanetur.  
Then treat it with ointments until it heals.  

Si autem times quod opiletur, tunc pone in foramine cannulam de plumbo diebus multis, et auferatur quando puer uult egerere.  
If you fear it may become obstructed, place a lead tube in the opening for many days, and remove it when the child wants to evacuate.  

Et iam accidit opilatio Ani etiam ex consolidatione uulneris, aut apostematis.  
Sometimes obstruction of the anus also occurs due to wound healing or an abscess.  

Oportet ergo ut secetur illa consolidatio, deinde curetur cum eo quod diximus ex curatione et plumbo.  
Therefore, that hardened area should be cut, then treated as we described, with healing and lead.  

¶ De curatione Fistularum quae accidunt in inferiori parte.  
On the treatment of fistulas occurring in the lower part.  

Caput LXXX.  
Chapter 80.  

Fistulae quae accidunt in inferiori, sunt Nodatio, et Grossitudo quae accidunt prope anum deforis: aut in spacio unius partium: et est Fistula una, aut plures.  
Fistulas that occur in the lower area are knotted growths and thicknesses that appear near the outside of the anus or in the space of one of the parts, and there may be one fistula or several.  

Cum ergo antiquatur illa Nodatio, aperitur, et currit ex ea humiditas aquosa alba, aut pus subtile.  
When this knotty growth becomes old, it opens, and a watery white moisture or thin pus flows from it.  

Et quandoque sunt ex istis Fistulis penetrantes.  
And sometimes these fistulas are penetrating.  

Ergo penetrantes cognoscuntur per illud quod egreditur ex egestione, et uentositate, quando utitur infirmus egestione: et fortasse egreditur ex eis uermis.  
Penetrating fistulas are recognized by the matter that exits with stools and gas when the patient evacuates; sometimes worms may emerge from them.  

Et sunt ex eis Fistulae quando sunt in spacio penetrantes usque ad uesicam, et usque ad meatum uirgae.  
Some fistulas, when they are in a certain position, penetrate as far as the bladder and to the urethra.  

Et sunt ex eis penetrantes usque ad iuncturam coxae, et usque ad nodum caudae.  
Some penetrate as far as the hip joint and to the coccygeal junction.  

Ex eo autem quo cognoscitur Fistula penetrans usque ad anum, etiam a non penetrante, est, ut intromittas digitum tuum indicem in anum: et intromittas tentam subtilem in Fistulam ex aere, aut ferro: quando non est tortuositas.  
To determine if a fistula penetrates to the anus, as opposed to a non-penetrating one, insert your index finger into the anus and a thin probe of brass or iron into the fistula when it is not twisted.  

Quod si in ea est tortuositas, tunc intromitte in eam tentam ex plumbo subtilem, aut pilum ex pilis equarum, donec sentias tentam, aut pilum in digito tuo.  
If there is a twist in it, then insert a thin lead probe into it, or a strand of horsehair, until you feel the probe or hair with your finger.  

Quod si non sentis ipsam penitus, neque procedit ex foramine aliquid ex egestione, neque uentositas, neque uermis sicut dixi: tunc scias, quia est non penetrans: propera ergo ad curationem.  
If you do not feel it at all, nor does anything exit from the opening with stool, nor gas, nor worms as I mentioned, then know that it is non-penetrating; proceed, therefore, with the treatment.

Et quando Fistula est penetrans usque ad uesicam, aut ad meatum urinae: tunc significatio eius est exitus urinae ex ea, et prohibitio eius ab hoc ut consolidetur locus cum medicinis.  
When the fistula penetrates to the bladder or the urinary tract, this is indicated by urine exiting from it, and it will resist healing with medication.

Si uero est penetrans usque ad iuncturam coxae, aut ad os coxae: tunc signum eius est, quod perueniat tenta usque illuc, si non est in ea tortuositas usque ad os: et inuentio doloris in circumitu partis, et quod egreditur pus ex ea semper: et quod non ualeat in ea medicatio, neque consolidatur cum unguento.  
If, however, it penetrates as far as the hip joint or the hip bone, the sign is that the probe reaches there without twisting, pain is felt around the area, pus constantly discharges from it, and it does not respond to medication or heal with ointments.

Et in istis Fistulis omnibus penetrantibus non est curatio omnino: et curatio earum est labor et uanitas ei, ex stultis medicis, super quem formatur.  
For all these penetrating fistulas, there is absolutely no cure, and treatment is merely labor and futility at the hands of foolish physicians who attempt it.

In illa autem quae non est penetrans, et non antiqua, speratur sanatio cum serro: secundum quod ego narro tibi, et ego iam probaui: et est, ut iaceat infirmus inter manus tuas super dorsum suum: et eleua crura eius usque supra coxas ipsius, et coxae eius sint inclinatae ad uentrem ipsius.  
For a fistula that is non-penetrating and not old, healing may be hoped for with a cautery, as I describe to you, having tested it myself. The patient should lie in your arms on his back, with his legs raised above his hips, and his hips bent toward his abdomen.

Deinde intromittetentam plumbi, aut aeris, si est in Fistula tortuositas, donec scias ubi peruenit tenta.  
Then, insert a lead or brass probe if there is twisting in the fistula, so you can determine how far the probe reaches.

Si autem sentit eam infirmus circa anum, tunc oportet ut intromittas digitum tuum indicem in anum.  
If the patient feels it near the anus, then you should insert your index finger into the anus.

Si ergo sentis in digito tuo tentam iam penetrasse per seipsam detectam, praeter quod sentias inter digitum tuum, et inter ipsum sifac, aut carnem: tunc ergo scias certe, quia est penetrans: non ergo labores in ea, quoniam non est eius sanatio, sicut diximus.
