If any moisture obstructs you, and there is no risk or error in cutting it, then incise the moisture and flesh, if they are there, and free the bones.

Si uero non est tibi praeparatio auferendi ossa ex hora tua, tunc pone super uulnus quod putrefaciat ipsum: et dimitte ipsum, donec putrefiat quod est in circumitu illorum ossium ex carnibus et humiditatibus.  
If you are not prepared to remove the bones immediately, then place on the wound something that will cause it to decay, and leave it until the flesh and moisture around those bones putrefy.

Et custodi uulnus ut non consolidetur.  
And keep the wound from closing.

Et constringatur sectio quam tu secuisti in operatione tua.  
And tighten the incision that you made in your operation.

Imo pone super ipsum, si times, cotum submersum sulfure trito cum oleo: aut cotum submersum in unguento aegyptio, aut aliquo unguentorum uiridium.  
Indeed, if you fear, place over it a cloth soaked in powdered sulfur with oil, or a cloth soaked in Egyptian ointment, or some green ointment.

Nam quando putrefient illae scilicet humiditates, et separantur ex eis ossa, alleuiatur ablatio eorum, et ipsorum attractio.  
For when those moistures putrefy and the bones separate from them, their removal and extraction is eased.

Si autem est os unum magnum, sicut os cruris, aut os coxae, et similia illis, et quod ex eo corruptum est, est pars magna: tunc rade ipsum rasione ultima, donec auferatur illa nigredo et corruptio.  
If it is a single large bone, such as the shin bone, or hip bone, or similar, and a large part of it is affected, then scrape it thoroughly until all blackness and corruption are removed.

Deinde restaura uulnus.  
Then restore the wound.

Si uero quod est in eo corruptum, est pars magna, et corruptio iam consecuta est medullam ossis, tunc necesse est serrare ipsum, et incidere ipsum totum usque ad locum, ubi peruenit corruptio: tunc cura ipsum, donec consolidetur.  
But if the affected part is large, and the corruption has already reached the bone marrow, then it is necessary to saw it and cut it completely up to the place where the corruption has reached; then treat it until it heals.

Et ego narro tibi zuken, quae accidit uiro in crure suo: ut ponas ipsam exemplum et adiutorium super operationem tuam.  
And I will tell you about a case of zuken that affected a man’s leg, so that you may use it as an example and aid in your operation.

Fuit uir iuuenis aetate circiter triginta annos, cui accidit dolor in crure suo, a caussa quae mota est super ipsum intra corpus, id est, ab interioribus, donec peruenerunt materiae ad crus, et apostematum est apostemate magno: et non fuit ei caussa extrinseca.  
There was a young man, about thirty years old, who experienced pain in his leg due to a cause originating within his body, that is, from internal sources, until the matter reached his leg, and a large swelling formed: and there was no external cause.

Extensum est ergo cum eo tempus cum errore medicorum, donec apertum est apostema, et concurrerunt cum eo materiae multae.  
Thus, a long time passed with the errors of the physicians, until the swelling was opened, and much matter collected in it.

Et postposita est curatio eius, donec fistulatum est crus, et facta sunt in eo orificia multa: quae omnia emittebant pus, et humiditates corporis.  
And his treatment was delayed until his leg developed fistulas, and many openings formed in it, all of which discharged pus and bodily moisture.

Curauit ergo ipsum multitudo medicorum circiter duos annos, et non fuit in eo sapiens in arte manus, donec uocatus sum, et uidi crus eius, et materias quae currebant ex illis orificiis cursu magno: etiam omne uiri corpus iam tabuerat, et color eius citrinus erat.  
Thus, many physicians treated him for about two years, but there was no skilled practitioner, until I was called, and I saw his leg and the matter flowing abundantly from those openings; the man’s whole body had already wasted away, and his complexion was yellowish.

Intromisi ergo tentam in uno locorum orificiorum, et peruenit tenta ad os.  
So I inserted a probe into one of the openings, and the probe reached the bone.

Deinde perscrutatus sum orificia omnia: et inueni ea peruenire ad se inuicem ex omnibus partibus cruris.  
Then I examined all the openings, and found them connecting with each other from all parts of the leg.

Properaui ergo, et secui super unum illorum orificiorum, donec detexi partem ossis: et inueni ipsum corruptum: quod iam corrosum erat, et denigratum, et putruerat, et perforatum erat, donec penetrauerat usque ad medullam.  
So I hastened and cut over one of those openings until I exposed part of the bone, and found it corrupted; it was already eaten away, blackened, rotten, and perforated, extending even into the marrow.

Serraui ergo quod detectum est mihi, et praeparatum ex osse corrupto.  
Therefore, I sawed off what I had uncovered, the corrupted part of the bone.

Et deputaui, quod non esset in osse nisi illa corruptio, quam abscidi, et serraui.  
And I determined that there was no other corruption in the bone except that which I had cut and sawed off.

Et ego iam eradicaueram eam.  
And I had already eradicated it.

Deinde posui restaurationem uulneris cum medicinis consolidatiuis spacio longo.  
Then I applied a restorative treatment to the wound with consolidating medicines for a long time.

Et non est consolidatum.  
But it did not heal.

Deinde tentaui, et detexi super os secundo supra detectionem primam: et inueni corruptionem continuam cum osse: et serraui quod apparuit mihi etiam ex illa corruptione.  
Then I probed, and exposed the bone a second time beyond the first exposure, and found further corruption in the bone; so I sawed off that portion of corruption as well.

Deinde conatus sum restaurationem eius.  
Then I attempted to restore it.

Et non est restauratum.  
But it was not restored.

Detexi ergo super ipsum iterum, et non cessaui incidere os particulatim, et conari restaurationem eius: et non est restauratum, donec incidi ex osse circiter palmum unum, et extraxi illud cum medulla sua.  
So I exposed it again, and continued cutting the bone piece by piece, and attempted to restore it; but it was not restored until I had cut off about one palm’s length of bone and removed it with its marrow.

Deinde restauraui ipsum cum medicinis, et consolidatum est uelociter, et sanatum: et non fuit necessaria haec iteratio in operatione eius, et sectione ipsius, nisi propter dispositionem debilitatis infirmi, et paucitatem tolerantiae eius, et timorem meum super ipsum de morte: quoniam accidebat ei in omnibus horis ex superfluitate euacuationis syncopis mala.  
Then I restored it with medicines, and it healed quickly and was cured; this repetition in his operation and cutting was necessary only because of the patient’s weakness, his limited tolerance, and my fear for his life, for he frequently suffered fainting spells from excessive drainage.

Sanatus est ergo sanatione integra: et nata est in loco ossis caro dura, et bona facta est dispositio in corpore suo, et rediit uirtus eius: et conuersatus est in dispositionibus suis: et non fecit ei contrarietatem in ambulatione nocumentum omnino.  
Thus, he was completely healed; hard flesh grew in the place of the bone, his body was restored to good condition, his strength returned, and he resumed his regular activities; walking posed no difficulty for him at all.

Si autem os eminens in loco corporis iam fractum est: tunc oportet ut serres ipsum, secundum hunc modum: et est: ut accipias ligamentum, et stringe ipsum in extremitate ossis eminentis: et praecipe alicui, qui extendat ipsum ad sursum: et pone ligamentum aliud ex lana grossius ligamento primo.  
But if a prominent bone in a part of the body is already fractured, then you must saw it as follows: take a band, and tie it at the end of the prominent bone, instruct someone to pull it upward, and place another band made of wool, thicker than the first band.

Deinde liga ipsum super carne, quae est suh osse: et extende extremitatem eius, ut trahas carnem ad inferiora: et tu detegis carnem super locum quem uis serrare, ut non laedat Serra carnem.  
Then tie it over the flesh beneath the bone, and extend its end to draw the flesh downward; and you expose the flesh over the area you wish to saw, so that the saw does not injure the flesh.

Pone lignum, aut tabulam sub osse inferius decenter: quoniam quando facis illud, non prohibetur quin secet carnem corruptam.  
Place a piece of wood or a board properly beneath the lower part of the bone, for when you do this, it prevents the saw from cutting the decayed flesh.

Et oportet ut sit Serratura super locum corruptum parumper, ut non sit in concauitate ossis corruptio: et non appareat in apparitione sua sensui, et cogat ad Serraturam sui uice alia.  
The sawing must be slightly above the corrupted area, so that no corruption remains within the hollow of the bone; and nothing should be visible to indicate the need for further sawing.

Quod si os est corruptum, et non est eminens, imo continuatur pars eius cum parte: et corruptio est in medio eius, aut in parte ipsius: tunc detege carnem ab omnibus partibus totam.  
But if the bone is corrupted and is not protruding, rather it continues from one part to another, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it, then expose all the flesh from all sides.

Deinde pone lignum inferius.  
Then place a piece of wood beneath it.

Postea serra illud ex parte prima, ubi est corruptio, donec continuetur Serratura ex parte altera: et sit Serratura secundum longitudinem a corruptione parumper, secundum quod diximus.  
Afterward, saw it from the first part where the corruption is, until the sawing continues to the other side; and let the sawing be slightly beyond the length of the corruption, as we have said.

Quod si corruptio est in iunctura, incide ipsam iuncturam corruptam, et serra os ubi continuatur ex parte altera.  
But if the corruption is in a joint, cut through that corrupted joint and saw the bone where it connects to the other side.

Si uero corruptio est in continuatione duarum iuncturarum, tunc non est in ea ingenium nisi abrasio.  
If the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, then the only solution is to abrade it.

Quod si corruptio est in pectine manus, aut in pectine pedis: tunc res in eo est difficilis ualde.  
If the corruption is in the palm of the hand or the sole of the foot, then the matter is exceedingly difficult.

Verum oportet, ut inquiras corruptionem qualiter appareat tibi.  
However, you must examine how the corruption appears to you.

Et abradas eam, et mundes ipsam secundum quamcunque dispositionem tibi possibile est, et cum quocunque ingenio rectificatur tibi: quando non facit tibi contrarietatem Vena, aut Neruus.  
And abrade it, and clean it by any method possible to you, and with whatever skill is appropriate for you, provided that no vein or nerve obstructs you.

Et scias quod incisoria, et Serrae ad incidendum ista ossa sunt multa, secundum situm ossium, et praparationem eorum, et ipsorum grossitudinem, et subtilitatem eorum, et magnitudinem, et paruitatem ipsorum, et duriciem ipsorum, et eorum raritatem.  
And know that the cutting instruments and saws for cutting these bones are many, depending on the position of the bones, their preparation, their thickness, their fineness, their size, their smallness, their hardness, and their sparseness.

Quapropter oportet, ut praepares omni speciei operationis instrumentum conueniens ad illam operationem.  
Therefore, you must prepare a suitable instrument for each type of operation.

Et scias, quod operationes istae significant tibi super speciem instrumenti quo indiges, quando tecum est studium longum.  
And know that these operations reveal to you the kind of instrument you need, when you engage in prolonged study.

Et cognitio modorum huius artis, testimonium modorum aegritudinum: tunc enim iam inuenies per teipsum illud quod conuenit ei ex instrumentis ad omnem infirmitatem.  
And knowledge of the methods of this art, through experience with various ailments, will enable you to find on your own the appropriate instrument for every affliction.

Et ego sum firmans tibi in ultimo huius capituli numerum instrumentorum, quae pones exempla super quae incides, et probationem qua experiaris super alia.  
And I am setting forth for you at the end of this chapter the number of instruments, which serve as examples for cutting, and the test by which you may apply them to other cases.

Forma Serrae.  
Form of the saw.

Forma alterius Serrae.  
Form of another saw.

Forma Serrae alterius.  
Form of yet another saw.

Forma Serrae alterius.  
Form of yet another saw.

Haec forma Serrae depicta, sit decenter facta.  
This form of the saw is depicted, let it be made properly.

Fiat arcus eius superior, acuitas eius ex ferro: et manubrium eius ex buxo, et sit pyramidale decenter factum.  
Let its upper arc be made, with sharpness from iron; its handle from boxwood, and let it be shaped like a pyramid, made properly.

Forma Rasorii iuncturarum.  
Form of a joint scraper.

Sit caput huius Rasorii, secundum formam capitis claui stellati: et puncta eius sint secundum formam punctorum elischetfegi.  
Let the head of this scraper be shaped like the head of a star-shaped nail, and its points like the points of an elischetfegi.

Et non conuenit, nisi ut fricentur cum eo capita iuncturarum, quando corrumpuntur, aut os amplum, et magnum est.  
And it is not suitable except for rubbing the heads of joints when they are corrupted, or when the bone is large and broad.

Forma maioris Rasorii.  
Form of a larger scraper.

Forma medii Rasorii.  
Form of a medium scraper.

Forma Rasorii lati.  
Form of a broad scraper.

Forma Rasorii in quo est concauitas.  
Form of a scraper with a hollow.

Forma Rasorii alterius subtilis.  
Form of another fine scraper.

Forma Rasorii alterius curuatae extremitatis.  
Form of another scraper with a curved end.

Forma Rasorii parui, subtilis tentae.  
Form of a small, fine probe scraper.

Forma Rasorii cum quo inciduntur ossa.  
Form of the scraper with which bones are incised.

Forma etiam Rasorii magni.  
Form of a large scraper as well.

Hoc similatur Radio, et extremitas est sicut Serra: exhibetur in locis multis ex rasione ossium.  
This is similar to a spoke, and the end is like a saw; it is displayed in many locations for bone scraping.

Forma Rasorii quod conuenit ad rasionem eius quod perforatum est ex ossibus.  
Form of the scraper suited for scraping perforated bones.

Extremitas eius triangula, acutarum est extremitatum.  
Its end is triangular, with sharp points.

Fit ex Indi.  
It is made from Indian steel.

Et similiter oportet, ut fiant omnia quae diximus ex Rasoriis, et Incisoriis, et Serris.  
And similarly, all the scrapers, cutters, and saws we have mentioned should be made accordingly.

¶ De incisione extremitatum, et Serratura ossium.  
On the cutting of extremities and the sawing of bones.

Caput LXXXIX.  
Chapter 89.

Putrefiunt extremitates, aut ex caussa extrinseca, aut intrinseca.  
Extremities decay either from an external or internal cause.

Cum ergo medicatus fueris illam corruptionem curatione medicinarum, et non confert curatio: et uides corruptionem incidere in membrum, quam non repercutit aliquid: tunc oportet ut incidas illud membrum usque ubi consequitu corruptio, ut euadat infirmus per illud a morte, aut a malicia quae est maior defectu membri.  
Therefore, when you have treated that corruption with medicines and the treatment does not help, and you see the corruption affecting a limb, which nothing repels, then it is necessary to cut that limb up to the point where the corruption has spread, so that the patient may escape death or a greater harm than the loss of the limb.

Et signum cui accidit illud est, quod denigratur membrum, donec putetur: quod ignis combussit ipsum, aut putrefit post nigredinem: donec inciditur illa putredo usque ad illud quod sequitur illud membrum, et serpit in totum corpus.  
The sign of this condition is that the limb blackens and putrefies, as if burned by fire, or decays after turning black; and this decay continues until it is cut to the point beyond the limb, and it spreads throughout the whole body.

Propera ergo cum incisione eius, et similiter si caussa corruptionis est a percussione quorundam uenenosorum: sicut scorpionis marini, et uiperae, et rutellae, et similium.  
Therefore, hasten to cut it, especially if the cause of the corruption is from the sting of certain venomous creatures, like the sea scorpion, viper, or rutella, and the like.

Si ergo corruptio, aut percussio est in extremitate digiti, tunc incide digitum, et non des spacium corruptioni, ut incedat usque ad reliquam manum.  
If the corruption or injury is in the tip of a finger, then cut off the finger, and do not give the corruption room to spread to the rest of the hand.

Et similiter si accidit in manu, tunc incide eam ex radice focilis, et non des spacium corruptioni, donec capiat in focili brachii.  
And likewise, if it occurs in the hand, then cut it off from the root of the wrist, and do not allow the corruption to spread until it reaches the joint of the arm.

Et si inuadit in eo, tunc incide brachium apud cubitum in iunctura sua.  
If it invades further, then cut the arm at the elbow at its joint.

Si autem pertransit corruptio, et uides eum circiter cubitum: tunc in illo est mors infirmi.  
But if the corruption spreads beyond, and you see it around the elbow, then that is where the patient’s death lies.

Et administrare praeter illud ex curatione, est quantitas uirtus.  
To apply treatment beyond this is a matter of strength.

Et similiter fac de pede, quando inuadit corruptio in digito, tunc incide ipsum apud unum nodorum: et si capit in pectine pedis, tunc incide pedem totum.  
Likewise, do the same with the foot; when the corruption invades a toe, then cut it at one of the joints; and if it reaches the sole of the foot, then cut off the whole foot.

Si autem ascendit ad genu, tunc incide crus apud iuncturam genu.  
If it reaches the knee, then cut the leg at the knee joint.

Quod si corruptio iam peruenit supra genu, tunc non est in ea ingenium, nisi dimissio, et relinquere infirmum morti.  
But if the corruption has already spread above the knee, then there is no remedy other than to leave the patient to die.

Et modus incidendi membrum, aut serrandi ipsum est, ut stringas ligamentum in inferiori, quem uis incidere: et stringe ligamentum aliud supra locum.  
The method of cutting or sawing a limb is to tie a band below the area you wish to cut, and another band above the place.

Et extendat minister ligamentum unum ad inferiora: et extendat minister aliud ligamentum superius ad sursum.  
Let an assistant pull one band downward, and another assistant pull the upper band upward.

Et tu separa carnem quae est inter duo ligamenta, cum Spatumili lato, donec detegatur caro tota.  
And you separate the flesh between the two bands with a wide spatula until all the flesh is exposed.

Deinde incidatur, aut serretur.  
Then it is to be cut or sawed.

Et oportet, ut ponas ab omnibus partibus pannum lini, et non tangat Serra locum sanum: et accidat infirmo laesio addita, et apostema calidum.  
It is necessary to place linen cloth all around, so that the saw does not touch the healthy area, which could cause the patient additional injury and a hot swelling.

Si autem accidat fluxus sanguinis interius dum operaris, tunc cauteriza locum uelociter: aut pone super ipsum quosdam pulueres abscindentes sanguinem.  
If there is internal bleeding during the operation, then cauterize the area quickly, or place on it some powders that stop bleeding.

Deinde redi ad medicationem tuam, donec compleatur.  
Then return to your treatment until it is complete.

Deinde liga membrum uulneratum cum ligamento conueniente ei, et cura ipsum, donec sanetur.  
Then bind the wounded limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it heals.

Et ego narro tibi quod accidit uiro in pede suo, hoc idem accidens quod narro tibi.  
And I will tell you what happened to a man’s foot, an instance of this same condition I am telling you about.

Quod est, quia accidit in pede suo nigredo, cum adustione quae assimilatur combustioni ignis: et corruptio illa in primis accidit in digito suo, donec coepit pedem totum.  
It happened that his foot became blackened, with a burning similar to that of fire; and at first the corruption affected his toe, until it affected the whole foot.

Properauit ergo uir ex seipso, postquam uidit corruptionem incidere in membro cum uehementia eius, quod inuenit ex dolore, et adustione eius: et incidit ipsum apud iuncturam, et sanatus est.  
The man hastened on his own, after seeing the corruption affecting his limb with such intensity, feeling it in the pain and burning; he cut it at the joint, and he was healed.

Et postquam praeteriit ei tempus longum, accidit ei illa eadem corruptio in digito manus suae indice.  
After a long time had passed, the same corruption occurred in his index finger.

Venit ergo ad me, et conatus sum recuperare illam superfluitatem cum eo quod posui super manum ex medicinis post mundificationem corporis eius: et non repercussa est superfluitas, et coepit incedere in digitum alium: donec coepit coruptio in manum.  
He came to me, and I tried to remove the excess with medicines I applied to his hand after cleansing his body; but the excess was not repelled, and it began to spread to another finger, until the corruption began to affect the hand.

Vocauit ergo me, ad incidendum manum eius: et nolui illud, sperans ex me super repercussionem illius superfluitatis: et timui etiam super ipsum apud incisionem manus eius mortem.  
He then called me to cut off his hand, but I did not want to, hoping that I could still repel the excess; and I also feared for his life at the thought of cutting off his hand.

Quoniam uirtus uiri erat super casum.  
For the man’s strength was nearly spent.

Postquam ergo desperauit de me, reuersus est ad terram suam: et peruenit ad me de eo, quia properauit, et incidit manum suam totam: et sanatus est.  
After he lost hope in me, he returned to his own land; and I received word that he hastened and cut off his entire hand, and he was healed.

Et non attuli hanc narrationem, nisi ut sit adiutorium super illud quod cadit de genere huius aegritudinis: et ut sit significatio qua significetur, et secundum quam agatur.  
I have recounted this story only so that it may serve as a guide for cases of this kind of illness, and as an example to follow and act upon accordingly.

¶ De cura Sinuum, et qualitate clisterizationis cum medicinis.  
On the treatment of sinuses, and the nature of enemas with medicines.

Caput XC.  
Chapter 90.

Quando accidit apostema in quibusdam membris carnosis, et prolongatur spacium apostematis, donec collectionem facit saniei: deinde rumpitur, aut perforatur, et egreditur quod in eo est ex sanie, et remanet locus uacuus quasi sit uas: et cutis quae est super ipsum sicut pannus qui iam subtiliatus est: et non peruenit ad ultimum in corruptione sua, neque imprimit in os, neque in neruum, neque in ligamentum: meretur ut nominetur Sinus: et non nominatur Fistula: uerumtamen si prolongatur spacium eius, donec imprimat corruptio in aliquid horum membrorum, tunc nominatur Fistula, aut zuken.
When an abscess occurs in certain fleshy members, and the duration of the abscess extends until it collects pus: then it bursts or is pierced, and what is inside it comes out as pus, and a hollow space remains as if it were a vessel: and the skin that is over it is like a cloth that has already been thinned, and it does not reach the deepest corruption, nor does it press on bone, nerve, or ligament: it deserves to be called a sinus and is not called a fistula: however, if its space extends until the corruption reaches one of these parts, then it is called a fistula or zuken.

Et cura eius est, ut incidas illam cutem totam sicut reuoluitur: et praecipue quando subtiliata est, et facta sicut pannus: et confidis quia non aaehaeret cum loco, propter corruptionem suam.
And its treatment is to cut all that skin as it is unfolded, especially when it has thinned and become like a cloth: and you are assured that it is not adhering to the place due to its corruption.

Si autem speras quod adhaereat cutis, et non consequitur ex eo corruptio illa ultima consecutione: et si in cute est spissitudo ex carne, tunc cura ipsum cum Clisteri: et est, ut consideres ad Sinum.  
If, however, you hope that the skin will adhere, and it does not result in that final corruption in consequence, and if there is thickness from flesh in the skin, then treat it with a clyster, and consider the sinus.

Tunc si est magnus, et pus quod emittitur ex eo est foetidi odoris: tunc clisteriza ipsum cum medicamine aegyptio, quod est aceti, et olei, et ziniar, partes recipiens aequales, aggregentur in uase: et decoquantur super ignem, donec rubeat medicamen: et ueniat in spissitudinem mellis.  
Then if it is large, and the pus discharged from it has a foul odor, then cleanse it with an Egyptian medicine, which is made of vinegar, oil, and ziniar, taking equal parts, placed in a vessel, and boiled over fire until the medicine becomes red and thickens like honey.

Deinde accipe ex eo quod tibi necesse est: et dissolue ipsum cum aqua et melle, et clisteriza cum eo Sinum: et stringe orificium eius, et dimitte medicinam in eo ad quantitatem duarum horarum.  
Then take from it what you need, and dissolve it with water and honey, and cleanse the sinus with it; tighten its opening, and leave the medicine in it for about two hours.

Deinde extrahe ipsum cum expressione: fac illud diebus tot, donec mundificetur Sinus, et remoueatur foetor.  
Then extract it with pressure; do this for as many days as necessary until the sinus is cleansed, and the foul odor is removed.

Et quandoque clisterizatur cum aqua cineris, quando non est tibi praesens hoc medicamen: et est, ut accipias cinerem lignorum uitis, aut cinerem ex lignis ilicis: et proiicias super eam aquam.  
And sometimes it is cleansed with ash water when this medicine is not available; take ash from vine wood or holm oak wood, and throw it over the water.

Deinde cola eam, et clisteriza cum ea, donec confidas quod Sinus iam ablutus est.  
Then strain it, and cleanse with it until you are confident that the sinus is now washed.

Quod si infirmo non est tolerantia super medicamen aegyptium, neque aquam cineris, tunc clisteriza ipsum cum aqua et melle, cui iam permixtum est aliquid ex ziniar contrito.  
If the patient cannot tolerate Egyptian medicine or ash water, then cleanse it with water and honey mixed with some crushed ziniar.

Aut clisteriza ipsum cum melle et uino permixtis, quoniam de proprietate mellis est, ut mundificet, et abluat: et uinum facit adhaerere Sinum, praecipue quando in uino est superfluitas stipticitatis et siccitatis.  
Or cleanse it with honey and wine mixed together, since honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and wine helps the sinus adhere, especially when the wine has an excess of astringency and dryness.

Cum facis illud aliquotiens, et confidis quod Sinus corruptio iam remota est: tunc clisteriza ipsum cum eo quod facit nasci carnem in eo.  
When you have done this several times, and are confident that the corruption in the sinus is now removed, then cleanse it with something that promotes flesh growth in it.

Et est, ut accipias ex emplastro dyafinicon: et dissoluas ipsum cum oleo rosato, et uino stiptico: aut clisteriza ipsum cum quibusdam medicinis, et unguentis aliis, quorum proprietates scripsi in tractatu unguentorum.  
This means you should take dyafinicon plaster and dissolve it with rose oil and astringent wine; or cleanse it with certain medicines and other ointments, the properties of which I have written in the treatise on ointments.

Quod si orificium Sinus est strictum, in quo non capit cannula clisteris: tunc amplifica ipsum cum ferro parumper: aut pone in ipso licinium inuolutum in unguento aegyptio, aut in unguento basilicon, donec amplificetur.  
If the opening of the sinus is narrow and does not admit the clyster tube, then enlarge it slightly with an iron tool; or place a linen strip soaked in Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment in it, until it expands.

Et similiter si est orificium etiam amplum, tunc aggrega labia eius cum sutura: et dimitte ex eo quantitatem in quam ingrediatur clistere sine additione.  
Similarly, if the opening is too wide, then draw its lips together with a suture, and leave enough space for the clyster to enter without any further addition.

Et similiter si orificium eius ex quo currit pus, est eleuatum ad superiora: tunc seca ipsum in depressiori loco qui est in ipso, ut currat ex eo pus usque inferius: quoniam pus quando coartatur in profunditate Sinus, prohibet carnem generari in eo.  
Likewise, if the opening from which pus flows is elevated above, then cut it at a lower point so that the pus flows downward, since pus, when confined in the depth of the sinus, prevents flesh from growing in it.

Quod si non est tibi possibile secare Sinum circiter inferius eius secundum quod uis: tunc conare, ut praepares membrum praeparatione qua currat ex eo pus cum facilitate secundum quod praeparatur tibi.  
If it is not possible for you to cut the sinus lower as you desire, then attempt to prepare the limb in a way that allows pus to flow from it easily according to your preparation.

Conare, ut non retineatur in eo aliquid ex pus omnino: et accipe medicinas consolidatiuas quae ponuntur super signum, conuenientes ad illud quod uis.  
Ensure that no pus at all is retained in it; and take healing medicines that are applied over the wound, appropriate for what you intend.

Et extende eas super pannum lini.  
And spread them over a linen cloth.

Et sit pannus tantae quantitatis, qua fiat communicatio totius Sinus.  
And let the cloth be of such size that it covers the entire sinus.

Deinde incide cum forficibus in directo orificii Sinus foramen, amplius orificio Sinus parumper.  
Then cut a hole with scissors directly at the opening of the sinus, slightly larger than the sinus opening.

Deinde extende ex unguentis lenibus super pannum alium, secundum quantitatem foraminis: et pone eum super ipsum positione longinqua ab orificio Sinus, ut alleuietur exitus pus ex eo: et non auferas pannum magnum, nisi post dies aliquos uice una.  
Then spread mild ointments over another cloth, according to the size of the hole, and place it over the area, keeping it slightly away from the sinus opening, to ease the exit of pus from it; and do not remove the large cloth except once after a few days.

Ille autem qui est super orificium Sinus, est ille quem remoues in omni hora, ut egrediatur quod aggregatur in eo ex pus: et ut scias, an illud quod currit ex eo uirus, est multum, aut parum: aut digestum, aut indigestum.  
But the one that is on the sinus opening is the one you remove every hour, to allow the pus that accumulates in it to flow out; and so you may know whether the discharge is copious or scant, digested or undigested.

Et cum hoc iterum considera locum Sinus ipsius, an in ipso sentiat dominus eius dolorem, aut non sit in eo dolor, et an sit in eo apostema, aut non sit in eo apostema.  
And with this, again consider the location of the sinus, whether its owner feels pain in it or there is no pain, and whether there is an abscess in it or not.

Cum ergo protenditur medicatio tua taliter, et uides materiam quae egreditur super orificium Sinus, tunc scias, quod Sinus iam adhaeret, aut approximat adhaerentiae: tunc ergo solue ipsum in mane, aut in tertio die: et quando soluis uulnus, tunc permuta pannum alium, et renoua unguentum.  
Therefore, when your treatment progresses in this manner, and you see material emerging from the sinus opening, then know that the sinus is already adhering or is close to adherence; then, release it in the morning or on the third day, and when you uncover the wound, replace the cloth and renew the ointment.

Si autem egreditur ex Sinu post spacium longum uirus subtile, tunc non desperes de adhaerentia eius, nam sanatio eius appropinquat, quoniam ex hominibus sunt qui tardant generationem carnis in uulneribus suis, et ex eis sunt qui agunt econtrario illius.  
However, if thin discharge comes out from the sinus after a long interval, then do not despair of its adhesion, for its healing is approaching, since among people, there are those who are slow in generating flesh in their wounds, and others who act contrary to this.

Si autem egreditur ex Sinu post dies multos pus indigestum, tunc scias quod sinus non adhaeret.  
But if undigested pus emerges from the sinus after many days, then know that the sinus is not adhering.

Si ergo tardatur adhaerentia Sinus, et prolongatur res eius: tunc adde in exiccatione medicinarum, uerum faciant medici, ut sint medicinae in substantia sua humidae, et in uirtute sua siccae: sicut unguentum dyafinicon, quando additur in eo superfluitas additionis ex zegi.  
Therefore, if the adhesion of the sinus is delayed and its matter is prolonged, then increase the drying quality of the medicines; let physicians make the medicines moist in substance but dry in their effect, like dyafinicon ointment, when an excess of zegi is added to it.

Et ex magis ultimo quo curatur, est, ut accipias unguentum dyafinicon, et soluatur cum oleo rosato, et roretur super ipsum uinum antiquum aequale in substantia sua.  
And among the more final treatments, take dyafinicon ointment, dissolve it with rose oil, and sprinkle it with old wine in equal measure.

Deinde confice ipsum cum eo, et utere ipso.  
Then prepare it with this and use it.

Et iam facit simile huic actioni, quando non est tibi praesens unguentum dyafinicon, mel, quando decoquis ipsum, donec ingrossetur, et uteris eo.  
And similar to this procedure, when dyafinicon ointment is not available, is honey, when you boil it until it thickens, and use it.

Aut accipe myrrham, et aloen, et olibanum: tere totum, et pulueriza illud super mel dum est super ignem.  
Or take myrrh, aloe, and frankincense; grind it all, and sprinkle it over honey while it is over the fire.

Deinde line super ipsum pannum, et stringe ipsum super Sinum: et line cum melle quod decoquisti, donec ingrossatum est: et pulueriza super ipsum species, et pone super ipsum pannum, et stringe eum.  
Then spread it on a cloth and bind it over the sinus; also spread it with the honey you boiled until thickened, sprinkle spices over it, place it on a cloth, and bind it.

Et quandoque administratur in illo aristolochia longa, et radices lilii coelestis, et est lilium: et farina herbi, et centaurea.  
And sometimes long aristolochia, and the roots of heavenly lily, which is a lily, and herb flour, and centaury are applied to it.

Utere eis simplicibus, aut aggregatis, tere ea, et cribella ipsa: et pulueriza super mel quod narraui, et utere eo.  
Use them simply or combined, grind them, sift them, and sprinkle them over the honey as I mentioned, and use it.

Quod si prolongatur res Sinus, et non sanatur hac curatione: tunc scias, quod in profundo eius est corruptio: aut iam facit impressionem in ossibus, aut in reliquis membris duris, aut ligamentis: tunc cura ipsum curatione Fistularum, secundum quod praemissum est.  
But if the matter of the sinus is prolonged and it is not healed by this treatment, then know that there is corruption in its depth, or it is already affecting the bones, or the other hard parts, or ligaments; then treat it with the cure for fistulas, as previously mentioned.

¶ De cura Panaritii et unguis attritae, et incisione digiti additi, et sectione.  
On the care of panaritium, injured nail, and incision of an extra finger, and section.

Caput XCI.  
Chapter 91.

Panaritium est apostema quod nascitur sub ungue pollicis manus, aut pedis: et fortasse nascitur in reliquis digitis.  
Panaritium is an abscess that forms under the nail of the thumb of the hand or foot, and perhaps it occurs on other fingers.

Cum ergo prolongatur res eius, et negligitur curato eius, et apostematur apostemate calido: aut corrumpitur, et emittit pus, donec corrodit radicem unguis: et fortasse corrumpit eam totam, et fortasse peruenit corruptio ad os, donec est ei odor foetidus: et fit extremitas digiti lata, et fit color eius fuscus.  
When its condition is prolonged, and treatment is neglected, it becomes a warm abscess or decays and releases pus, until it corrodes the nail root; it may destroy it entirely, and sometimes the decay reaches the bone, producing a foul odor, and the tip of the finger becomes swollen and dark-colored.

Quando ergo tu curas ipsum, cum eo quod diximus in diuisione, et non confert curatio tua: tunc oportet ut incidas cum ferro totam superfluitatem quae remansit ex ungue.  
When you are treating it as we described in the previous section, and your treatment is not effective, then you must cut away with an iron all the excess that remains of the nail.

Deinde cauteriza uulnus post illud.  
Then cauterize the wound afterward.

Cauterium enim iuuatiuum est ualde.  
For cauterization is very helpful.

Si uero os est sanum, et est unguis etiam sana, et additiones uacuae unguis iam comprimunt carnem ad interiora, et incipiunt pungere ipsam, et laedunt eam: tunc oportet ut ponas Radium subtilem sub angulo unguis quae pungit carnem, et impelle eam sursum: et incide eam carnem cum facilitate, et pone super illud quod remanet de carne ex medicinis comburentibus, corrosiuis, donec remoueatur totum eius.  
If, however, the bone is sound and the nail is also healthy, and the empty extensions of the nail press the flesh inward, begin to prick it, and injure it, then you should place a thin stick under the angle of the nail that pricks the flesh and push it upward; cut away the flesh with ease, and apply burning or corrosive medicines to what remains of the flesh until all of it is removed.

Deinde cura illud cum unguentis, donec sanetur.  
Then treat it with ointments until it heals.

Si autem corruptio iam imprimit in os, tunc oportet ut incidas illud os, et extrahas ipsum: non enim sanatur unquam dum permanet in eo os corruptum.  
But if the decay has already affected the bone, then you must cut away that bone and remove it, for it will never heal as long as the corrupted bone remains.

Quod si uides corrosionem et corruptionem incedere in digitum, tunc incide eum in uno nodorum, secundum quod praemissa est eius rememoratio.  
If you see the corrosion and decay spreading into the finger, then cut it at one of the joints, as previously described.

Deinde cura ipsum, donec sanetur.  
Then treat it until it heals.

Si autem accidat ungui attritio, aut percussio: et contingit in ea dolor uehemens, tunc oportet ut phlebotomes infirmum in primis.  
If the nail is damaged or struck, causing intense pain, then first it is necessary to perform phlebotomy on the patient.

Deinde seca unguem cum Spatumili acuto sectione transuersa de sursum ad uisum.  
Then cut the nail with a sharp spatula in a transverse incision from above toward the visible part.

Et custodi, ne sectio perueniat ad carnem quae est sub ungue, nam tu facies accidere per illud super infirmum dolorem uehementem, et erit caussa ad natiuitatem carnis additae in loco.  
Be careful not to let the incision reach the flesh under the nail, for you would cause intense pain for the patient and lead to the growth of extra flesh in that spot.

Deinde cura locum cum eo quod sedat dolores.  
Then treat the area with something that soothes pain.

Digitus uero additus qui nascitur in quibusdam manibus hominum, fortasse est carnosus totus: et fortasse sunt in quibusdam eorum ossa, et fortasse est in eo unguis: et quidam eorum nascitur in radice iuncturae, aut est natiuitas eius in quibusdam nodis digiti.  
An extra finger, which appears in some people's hands, may be entirely fleshy, or in some cases contain bones, or may even have a nail; and some grow from the root of a joint or originate at certain joints of the finger.

Ille ergo qui nascitur in quibusdam nodis digiti, non mouetur: et ille qui nascitur apud iuncturam digiti, fortasse mouetur.  
One that grows at certain finger joints is immobile, while one that grows near a finger joint may be mobile.

Eius ergo qui ex eis est carnosus, sectio eius facilis est.  
Thus, the section of those that are fleshy is easy.

Quod est, ut incidas ipsum apud radicem suam cum Spatumili lato.  
That is, to cut it at its root with a broad spatula.

Eius autem cuius natiuitas est in radice iuncturae curatio, est difficilis.  
However, the treatment of one that originates at the root of a joint is difficult.

Abstine ergo ab incisione eius.  
Therefore, refrain from incising it.

In illo uero qui nascitur in digito apud ultimum nodorum, tunc oportet ut incidas in primis carnem eius incisione rotunda usque ad os.  
But for one that grows on the finger near the last joint, you should first cut its flesh in a circular incision down to the bone.

Deinde serra os cum una illarum Serrarum conuenientium ad illud.  
Then saw the bone with one of those saws suited for it.

Deinde cura ipsum, donec sanetur.  
Then treat it until it heals.

Consolidatio autem quae accidit digitis adinuicem, multotiens accidit aut ex natiuitate hominis, id est, nascitur cum eo, aut a consolidatione uulneris, aut combustione ignis, et similibus.  
Fusion of the fingers, which often occurs either by birth — that is, they are born with it — or by the healing of a wound, or by burning with fire, and similar causes.

Oportet ergo ut seces illam consolidationem, donec redeant digiti secundum formam suam naturalem.  
It is necessary, therefore, to cut that fusion until the fingers return to their natural shape.

Deinde pone inter eos licinia, aut pannos infusos in oleo rosato: ut non consolidentur uelociter, et separa inter eos: aut pone inter eos laminam plumbi subtilem, donec consolidetur locus secundum quod oportet.  
Then place linen strips or cloths soaked in rose oil between them, so they do not fuse again quickly, and keep them separated; or place a thin lead sheet between them until the area consolidates as needed.

Et similiter si accidat consolidatio quibusdam digitis cum palma, tunc seca illam consolidationem, secundum quod praeparatur et conuenit figurae membri.  
Similarly, if some fingers are fused with the palm, then cut that fusion according to what is prepared and suited to the shape of the limb.

¶ De incisione Vitium.  
On the incision of the disease.

Caput XCII.  
Chapter 92.

Uites sunt Venae inuolutae, grossae, plenae superfluitatibus melancholicis quae accidunt in pluribus membris corporis: et plurimum euentus earum est in cruribus, praecipue in cruribus iter agentium et laborantium, et portantium.  
Veins are twisted, thick, and full of melancholic superfluities that appear in various parts of the body: and mostly, they occur in the legs, especially in those who travel, labor, and carry loads.

Oportet ergo ut administres excussionem corporis ex cholera nigra aliquotiens excussione forti.  
Therefore, it is necessary to administer an expulsion of black bile from the body with a strong expulsion at times.

Deinde phlebotoma patientis eas basilicam.  
Then perform a phlebotomy on the basilic vein of the patient.

Curatio uero earum cum ferro, est secundum duos modos.  
Their treatment with iron is in two ways.

Vnus eorum est, ut secentur, et extrahatur sanguis niger.  
One of these is that they should be cut, and black blood should be extracted.

Et modus alter est, ut eleuetur Vena, et extrahatur tota.  
The other way is to elevate the vein and remove it entirely.

Sectio uero eius est secundum hunc modum.  
The cutting of it is in this manner.

Embroca crus in primis cum aqua calida multum, donec resoluatur sanguis grossus faeculentus.  
First, soak the leg with a lot of hot water until the thick, foul blood is dissolved.

Deinde stringe crus infirmi a superiori parte coxae eius, usque ad inferiorem partem genu cum uitta.  
Then bind the patient's leg from the upper part of the thigh down to the lower part of the knee with a band.

Deinde seca uenam in loco uno, aut duobus, aut tribus sectione ampla.  
Then cut the vein in one, two, or three places with a wide incision.

Deinde eleua, id est, extrahe sanguinem in manu tua ab inferiori parte cruris, usque ad sursum, et a superiori oportet ut phlebotomes infirmum in primis.  
Then lift, that is, extract the blood with your hand from the lower part of the leg upward, and from the upper part perform a phlebotomy on the patient initially.

Deinde seca unguem cum usque inferius: donec egrediatur ex sanguine quantitas quam uides sufficere, et quam tolerat uirtus infirmi.  
Then cut down to the nail until an amount of blood comes out that you see as sufficient and within the tolerance of the patient's strength.

Postea liga eam: et praecipe ei, ut abstineat a cibis generantibus choleram nigram: et itera euacuationem et phlebotomiam, quando implentur Venae, et nocet illud infirmo.  
Afterward, bind it, and instruct the patient to abstain from foods that generate black bile: and repeat the evacuation and phlebotomy when the veins are filled, and this harms the patient.

Eleuatio autem eius est secundum hunc modum.  
Its elevation is in this way.

Rade crus infirmi, si in ea sunt pili multi.  
Shave the patient’s leg if there are many hairs on it.

Deinde intromitte ipsum in balneum: aut embroca ipsum in crure eius cum aqua calida, donec rubeat, et exuberentur Venae: aut exercitetur exercitio forti, si non est ei praesens balneum, donec calefiat membrum.  
Then immerse it in a bath, or bathe it with hot water on the leg until it reddens and the veins swell, or have the patient engage in vigorous exercise if a bath is not available until the limb is heated.

Deinde seca cutem in directo uenae sectione per longitudinem: aut in ultimo eius apud genu, aut in inferiori parte eius apud calcaneum.  
Then cut the skin along the vein in a longitudinal section, either at its end near the knee or in its lower part near the heel.

Deinde aperi cutem cum uncinis, et excoria uenam ab omni parte, donec appareat sensui: et est apud apparitionem eius, quod uides eam rubeam ad nigredinem decliuem.  
Then open the skin with hooks and strip the vein on all sides until it becomes visible to touch: and upon its appearance, you see it red with a blackish tint.

Cum ergo uadit ex cute, uides eam albam quasi sit chorda.  
When it thus goes out from the skin, you see it white as if it were a cord.

Deinde intromitte sub ea Radium, donec quando eleuatur et egreditur de cute: suspende eam cum uncino caeco, leni.  
Then insert a probe beneath it, so that when it is elevated and exits the skin, suspend it with a gentle, blunt hook.

Deinde seca sectionem aliam prope illam sectionem tribus digitis.  
Then make another incision near that incision, three fingers apart.

Deinde excoria cutem a superiori parte uenae, donec appareat.  
Then strip the skin from the upper part of the vein until it becomes visible.

Deinde eleua eam cum Radiis sicut fecisti, et suspende eam cum uncino alio, sicut fecisti in primis.  
Then elevate it with probes as you did before and suspend it with another hook as you did initially.

Deinde seca sectionem aliam, aut sectiones plures, si indiges illo.  
Then cut another incision, or several incisions, if needed.

Deinde eleua, et incide ipsam ultima sectione apud calcaneum.  
Then elevate and cut it with a final incision near the heel.

Deinde extrahe eam ad sectionem quae est supra eam.  
Then draw it out to the section that is above it.

Et fac illud, donec extrahas eam ex sectione quae est superior, uel altior sectionibus omnibus, donec quando egreditur tota: tunc incide eam.  
And do this until you extract it from the section that is higher, or from all the incisions, until it is fully drawn out: then cut it.

Si autem non obedit tibi ad extrahendum, et eleuandum: tunc intromitte acum cum filo forti duplo, et liga eam, et extrahe ipsam: aut intromitte sub ea Radium: et reuolue manum tuam ad omnem partem, donec egrediatur.  
But if it does not respond to extraction and elevation, then insert a needle with a strong doubled thread, tie it, and pull it out, or insert a probe beneath it, and turn your hand to every side until it comes out.

Et caue, ne incidatur.  
And be careful not to cut it.

Nam si incidatur, fit difficile tibi eleuare eam ualde, et ingreditur super infirmum ex ea nocumentum.  
For if it is cut, it becomes very difficult to elevate, and it causes harm to the patient.

Cum ergo extraxeris eam totam: tunc pone super locum uulnerum lanam submersam in uino et oleo rosato, aut oleo: et cura ipsum, donec sanetur.  
When you have extracted it entirely, place wool soaked in wine and rose oil, or oil, over the wounds, and treat the patient until healed.

Quod si Vitis est contracta, habens tortuositatem cui sit inuolutio ad partes, et non est sicut diximus secundum rectitudinem: tunc oportet ut findas super eam ad omnem partem tortuositatis eius, et loca inuolutionis ipsius.  
But if the vein is contracted, having twists and bends, and is not as we have said in a straight line, then it is necessary to cut it over each twist and bend.

Deinde suspende eam cum uncinis, donec eleues eam totam: et caue apud sectionem tuam super eam ne incidas uenam, aut uulneres: nam difficile fiet super te eleuare, uel extrahere eam.  
Then suspend it with hooks until you elevate it entirely, and be careful near your incision on it not to cut or injure the vein, for it will become difficult for you to elevate or extract it.

Conserua ergo prudentiam tuam.  
Therefore, maintain your caution.

Forma Incidentis quo sanatur Vitis.  
The form of the incision by which the vein is healed.

Forma Vncini caeci.  
The form of the blunt hook.

Non est ei curuitas sicut reliquis Vncinis, neque est acutae extremitatis, ut non uulneret uenam: et est grossae flectuositatis, lenis: quoniam si esset subtilis, incideret uenam subtilitate sua: imo sit ei superflua grossitudo, sicut diximus.  
It does not have the curve like other hooks, nor a sharp end, so as not to wound the vein; it is thick and smooth, for if it were slender, it would cut the vein by its thinness; indeed, let it have extra thickness, as we have said.

De extractione Venae cruris.  
On the extraction of the vein of the leg.

Caput XCIII.  
Chapter 93.

Haec Vena generatur in cruribus in terris calidis, sicut Alizegi, et terra Arabum, et in terris aridis, calidis, paucae teneritatis, id est, in quibus non nascitur herba, neque arbor.  
This vein forms in the legs in hot lands, like Alizegi, the land of the Arabs, and in dry, hot lands with little tenderness, that is, where no grass or trees grow.

Et fortasse generatur in locis aliis corporis praeter crura.  
And it may perhaps form in other places of the body besides the legs.

Et generatio quidem eius est a putrefactione quae accidit sub cute, sicut accidunt intra corpora serpentes et uermes ascarides, et uermes generati inter cutem et carnem.  
Its formation indeed is due to decay that occurs beneath the skin, similar to how serpents and ascarid worms occur within bodies and worms form between the skin and flesh.

Et signum incaeptionis euentus huius Venae est, quod accidit in crure inflammatio uehemens.  
The sign of the beginning of this vein’s formation is that a violent inflammation occurs in the leg.

Deinde uesicatur locus.  
Then the area becomes blistered.

Deinde incipit Vena exire ex loco illius uesicationis, quasi sit radix plantae, aut animal.  
Then the vein begins to emerge from the site of that blistering, as if it were the root of a plant or an animal.

Cum ergo apparet ex ea extremitas eius, tunc oportet ut inuoluas super ipsam frustum plumbi, cuius pondus sit ex drachma keil, usque ad drachmas II et noda ipsam: et dimitte plumbum suspensum ex crure.  
When its end appears, you must wrap around it a piece of lead weighing from one to two drachmas, and knot it, letting the lead hang from the leg.

Quotiens ergo egreditur ex ea aliquid ad exteriora, inuolue illud in plumbo, et noda illud.  
Thus, whenever something from it comes outward, wrap it in lead and knot it.

Quod si prolongatur multum, tunc incide partem eius, et inuolue residuum.  
If it becomes too long, then cut part of it and wrap the remainder.

Et non incidas eam radicitus antequam egrediatur tota.  
And do not cut it at the root before it is entirely extracted.

Quoniam si incidis, contrahitur, et ingreditur in carnem: et facit accidere apostema, et putredinem in loco, et ulcus malum.  
For if you cut it, it contracts and goes into the flesh, causing an abscess, decay in the area, and a bad ulcer.

Quapropter oportet, ut suauiter tractetur, et extrahatur paulatim, donec egrediatur ex ultimo sui, et non remaneat ex ea aliquid in corpore: et ex hac quidem Vena egreditur in quibusdam hominibus quod est in longitudine sua quinque palmorum et decem.  
Therefore, it must be handled gently and extracted gradually until its very end is reached, leaving nothing of it in the body; in some people, this vein emerges with a length of five and ten palms.

Et iam peruenit ad me, quia exiuit uiro ex XX palmis.  
It has even been reported to me that it came out twenty palms long in one man.

Si autem inciditur tibi in hora medicationis tuae: tunc intromitte radium in foramine eius, et perfora eam foramine longo, cum corpore, donec euacuetur totum quod est in ea ex materia: et administra putrefactionem loci cum medicinis diebus aliquot.  
If it is cut during your treatment, then insert a probe into its hole, pierce it with a long opening, along with the body, until all the matter within is evacuated, and treat the decay in the area with medicines for a few days.

Deinde cura ipsum curatione apostematum.  
Then treat it as you would for abscesses.

Et haec quidem Vena quandoque habet ramos multos, praecipue quando apparet in iunctura pedis, aut in pede ipso: et accidunt ei orificia multa, et egreditur ex omni orificio ramus.  
This vein sometimes has many branches, especially when it appears at the joint of the foot or in the foot itself, and it has many openings, with a branch emerging from each opening.

Cura ergo ipsam, sicut diximus in diuisione, et cum eo quod praemissum est.  
Therefore, treat it as we have described in the section, and with what has been previously stated.

¶ De sectione super Vermes generatos sub cute, et dicitur Aegritudo bouina.  
On the incision for worms generated under the skin, called the "Bovine Disease."

Caput XCIIII.  
Chapter 94.

Haec Aegritudo nominatur in quadam terra apud nos Aegritudo bouina: propterea, quia multotiens accidit bouibus, et est uermis paruus unus, qui nascitur inter cutem et carnem.  
This disease is called the "Bovine Disease" in a certain land among us, because it often occurs in cattle, and it is a small worm that forms between the skin and flesh.

Et uadit in corpore toto, ascendendo et descendendo: et ostenditur sensui apud ambulationem eius de membro ad membrum, donec disrumpit ubicumque disrumpit in cute locum, et egreditur.  
And it moves throughout the whole body, ascending and descending, and becomes perceptible as it moves from one limb to another, until it eventually breaks through the skin and emerges wherever it ruptures.

Et generatio eius est ex putredine quorundam humorum.  
Its formation is due to the decay of certain humors.

Sicut accidunt uermes et serpentes, id est, lumbrici, et ascarides in uentre.  
Just as worms and serpents, that is, roundworms and ascarids, occur in the belly.

Et timetur ex malicia eius.  
It is feared for its malignancy.

Quia quando ipse uadit in corpore, et eleuatur ad caput, et peruenit ad locum: tunc fortasse aperit in eo, et egreditur, et destruit oculum: et accidit illud multotiens.  
For when it moves through the body and rises to the head, and reaches a place, it may rupture there, emerge, and destroy the eye; this happens frequently.

Cum ergo uis curare eum, et extrahere ipsum, tunc non fit illud nisi apud ambulationem eius, et apparitionem ipsius sensui.  
Therefore, when you wish to treat and remove it, this can only be done when it is moving and visible to the senses.

Oportet ergo, ut stringas quod est supra eum, et quod est sub eo cum ligamento constrictione forti.  
You must therefore bind tightly above and below it with a constricting band.

Deinde seca super ipsum, et extrahe eum.  
Then make an incision over it and extract it.

Quod si profundatur in carne, et non inuenis ipsum: tunc pone super locum cauterium cum igne, donec moriatur.  
But if it is deep in the flesh and cannot be found, then apply a cautery with fire over the area until it dies.

Et maius quod timetur, est corruptio eius, qua corrumpit oculum, sicut diximus.  
The greatest fear is its corruption, by which it destroys the eye, as we have mentioned.

Si autem uides eum iam peruenisse in capite prope oculum, tunc stringe sub eo supercilium strictura bona.  
If you see it has already reached the head near the eye, then bind tightly beneath it with a strong constriction on the eyebrow.

Deinde seca super ipsum, et extrahe eum.  
Then make an incision over it and extract it.

Et oportet ut utatur infirmus mundificatione sui corporis, cum medicinis soluentibus humores putridos malos.  
The patient must cleanse their body with medicines that dissolve foul, putrid humors.

Et caueat sibi a cibis generantibus putrefactionem.  
And they should avoid foods that cause decay.

¶ De sectione super aegritudinem Nakir.  
On the incision for the disease Nakir.

Caput XCV.  
Chapter 95.

Haec aegritudo nominatur in terra nostra Nakir: et est dolor qui accidit in quibusdam membris: deinde permutatur de membro ad membrum.  
This disease is called Nakir in our land, and it is a pain that occurs in certain limbs, then shifts from one limb to another.

Et ego quidem iam uidi ipsum, secundum quod narro tibi.  
And I have indeed seen it, as I will tell you.

Vocatus sum ad mulierem infirmam in quibusdam uillis.  
I was called to an ailing woman in a certain village.

Et detexit brachium suum, et uidi inflationem paruam in uena funis brachii.  
She uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm cord.

Et postquam remansi hora una, uidi unam inflationem incedere cum focili, sicut incedit uermis, ascendendo ad humerum eius uelocius quam esse potest: ut sit sicut argentum uiuum, quando currit de loco ad locum.  
After remaining there for an hour, I saw a swelling moving along like a worm, ascending to her shoulder faster than can be believed, like quicksilver running from one place to another.

Recessit ergo dolor ex illo loco, et fixus est in humero.  
The pain then left that area and became fixed in the shoulder.

Deinde sedi hora una, et cucurrit in reliquum corpus, donec perueniret in brachium aliud.  
Then, after sitting for another hour, it ran into the rest of the body, until it reached the other arm.

Deinde narrauit mihi, quia reuoluebatur in toto corpore suo, secundum quod uidi.  
Then she told me that it moved throughout her whole body, as I had seen.

Miratus sum ergo de uelocitate permutationis eius de membro ad membrum.  
I was amazed at the speed of its movement from one limb to another.

Et ego quidem ante illud non uideram hanc aegritudinem oculis meis taliter secundum hunc modum.  
I had not seen this illness with my own eyes in such a manner before.

Verumtamen uidi multos, qui inueniunt dolorem permutari de membro ad membrum: et non uidi ipsum oculis, sicut uidi eum in muliere.  
However, I have seen many who experience pain moving from limb to limb, though I had not seen it with my eyes as I did in this woman.

Et ego non cogito illud esse, nisi quod est propterea, quod mulier fuit ex illis qui sunt ex uillis sicci corporis detectarum uenarum: hinc ergo apparet sensui illa uentositas permutata.  
And I do not think this is the case unless it is because the woman was from those villages of people with dry bodies and exposed veins; thus, this shifting windiness appears to the senses.

Et est necesse, ut non appareant secundum hanc rationem in illis qui sunt deliciosi, et corporibus humidis, occultarum uenarum.  
And it is necessary that this does not appear in those who are indulgent, with moist bodies and hidden veins.

Cum ergo uis curationem eius, et sentit patiens illud dolorem: tunc si est apparens tibi oculo, sicut diximus, tunc stringe supra ipsum, et sub ipso uelociter: et seca supra ipsum, donec egrediatur illa uentositas coartata: et cauteriza locum.  
Therefore, when you wish to treat it and the patient feels the pain, if it is visible to you, as we have said, then bind tightly above and below it quickly; make an incision over it until the confined windiness exits, and cauterize the area.

Si autem non uides ipsum oculis tuis: tunc cura ipsum cum excussione corporis, et cum eo quod expellit uentositates, et carminat eas cum pillulis foetidis, et pillulis de serapino, et similibus.  
But if it is not visible to your eyes, then treat it with body evacuation, and with what expels windiness, and soothes it with foul-smelling pills and pills of serapinum, and the like.

¶ De extractione Sagittarum.  
On the extraction of arrows.

Caput XCVI.  
Chapter 96.

Sagittae diuersificantur secundum species suas, et secundum loca in quibus cadunt ex corpore.  
Arrows vary according to their types and according to the places in the body where they lodge.

Earum uero diuersitas est: quoniam ex eis sunt quae habent cuspides magnos, et paruos: et concauae, et surdae.  
Their diversity is as follows: for among them are those that have large and small points, and those that are concave and deaf.

Et ex eis sunt quae habent tres angulos.  
And among them are those that have three edges.

Et ex eis quibus sunt linguae.  
And among them are those with tongues.

Et ex eis quibus sunt astellae.  
And among them are those with stars.

Illae uero quae sunt secundum membra in quibus cadunt, est secundum duos modos.  
Those that lodge in certain parts of the body fall into two categories.

Aut enim membra sunt ex membris principalibus concauis, sicut cerebrum, et cor, et epar, et pulmo, et renes, et intestina, et uesica, et eis similia.  
Either they are in the principal hollow organs, such as the brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar parts.

Quando ergo cadit in aliquo horum membrorum, et apparent tibi signa mortis, quae ego narro tibi post, tunc oportet ut deuites extractionem illius sagittae ex eis, nam mors consequitur illum in quo est, in pluribus dispositionibus.  
Therefore, when it lodges in any of these parts, and signs of death appear to you, which I will tell you later, you must avoid extracting that arrow from them, for death follows in most cases.

Et quando non apparent tibi ista signa mala, et sagitta non est absconsa in profunditate membri, tunc extrahe ipsam, et cura uulnus.  
And when these evil signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not hidden in the depth of the part, then extract it and treat the wound.

Ex signis enim cerebri quando cadit in eo sagitta, et penetrat os, et egreditur siphac quod est super cerebrum, est: quoniam accidunt ex illo soda uehemens, et scotomia, et uertigo, et rubedo in oculis, et inflatio, et rubedo linguae, et spasmus, et permixtio intellectus, et uomitus cholerae.  
Among the signs of the brain when an arrow lodges there, and it penetrates the bone, and the membrane over the brain emerges, are these: sudden seizures, dizziness, vertigo, redness in the eyes, swelling, redness of the tongue, spasms, mental confusion, and vomiting of bile.

Et fortasse egreditur sanguis ex naribus, aut auribus.  
And sometimes blood comes out from the nose or ears.

Et fortasse abscinditur sermo, et destruitur uox.  
And sometimes speech is cut off, and the voice is destroyed.

Et egreditur ex loco uulneris humiditas alba similis pulti.  
And a white moisture similar to porridge comes out of the wound site.

Et exit ex eo simile aquositati carnis.  
And something similar to the watery discharge of flesh exits from it.

Si ergo apparent tibi ista signa, tunc abstine a curatione, et extrahe sagittam si non egreditur.  
If these signs appear to you, then refrain from treatment, and extract the arrow if it does not come out.

Signa autem sagittae quando cadit in corde, sunt: quod ipsa est prope mammillam sinistram: et sentit cum ea quasi ipsa sit fixa in re dura, non in re uacua.  
The signs of an arrow when it lodges in the heart are that it is near the left nipple, and it feels as if it is fixed in a hard object, not in an empty one.

Et fortasse sagittae est motus similis motui pulsus: et currit ex uulnere sanguis niger.  
And sometimes the movement of the arrow resembles the beat of a pulse, and black blood flows from the wound.

Et sequitur illud frigus extremitatum, et sudor frigidus, et syncopis.  
And coldness of the extremities follows, along with cold sweat and fainting.

Scias ergo, quod mors descendit procul dubio.  
Know, therefore, that death approaches without a doubt.

Et signum sagittae quando uulnerat pulmonem, est exitus sanguinis spumosi ex uulnere: et uasa quae sequuntur collum, apostematur, et mutatur color infirmi.  
The sign of an arrow wounding the lung is foamy blood coming from the wound, and the vessels following the neck become inflamed, and the patient's color changes.

Et expirat spiritum magnum, altum: et quaerit attractionem aeris frigidi.  
And he breathes a deep, high breath, and seeks the attraction of cold air.

Quod si cadat sagitta in uelamen, quod est in pectore: tunc est prope costas paruas: et fit anhelitus magnus cum dolore uehementi, cum suspirio: et mouentur omnia membra humerorum.  
But if the arrow lodges in the membrane in the chest, then it is near the small ribs, and there is great shortness of breath with intense pain, with sighing, and all the muscles of the shoulders move.

Et si cadat sagitta in stomachum, tunc fortasse egreditur ex uulnere ex cibo aliquid indigestum.  
And if the arrow lodges in the stomach, then perhaps something undigested exits from the wound.

Et si cadit sagitta in Ventrem, et figitur in eo: egreditur aliquid stercoris ex uulnere, aut zirbum, aut intestinum quod iam disruptum est.  
And if the arrow lodges in the abdomen and sticks there, something of feces exits from the wound, or bile, or intestine that is already ruptured.

Non est ergo spes in curatione eius, neque in extractione sagittae.  
Therefore, there is no hope in curing it, nor in extracting the arrow.

Quod si sagitta cadat in Vesicam, et egrediatur urina: et procedit ex ea aliquid ad exteriora, et fortior sit dolor super infirmum: tunc scias, quia est mortale.  
But if the arrow lodges in the bladder and urine comes out, and something proceeds from it to the outside, and the pain is stronger over the afflicted, then know that it is fatal.

Reliqua autem membra, sicut facies, et collum, et guttur, et spatula, et adiutorium, et spondiles dorsi, et furcula, et coxa, et crus, et eis similia ex membris saluantur secundum plures dispositiones: quando non inuenit sagitta arteriam, aut neruum: et non est sagitta uenenosa.  
However, the remaining parts, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, auxiliary part, spinal vertebrae, clavicle, hip, leg, and similar parts of the body are preserved in most cases, as long as the arrow does not hit an artery or nerve and is not poisonous.

Et ego narro tibi quod uidi de esse harum sagittarum, ut significes per illud super curationem tuam.  
And I tell you what I have observed concerning these arrows, so that you may apply it in your practice.

Quod est, quia cuidam uiro cecidit sagitta in lachrymali oculi eius, in radice nasi.  
For instance, an arrow fell into a man’s tear duct at the root of his nose.

Extraxi ergo eam ipsi ex parte altera, sub adipe auris eius: et sanatus est, et non accidit ei in oculo eius nocumentum.  
I therefore extracted it for him from the other side, under the fat of his ear, and he was healed, and no harm occurred to his eye.

Et extraxi sagittam aliam Iudaeo, quae cecidit ei in adipe oculi sui sub palpebra inferiori: et sagitta iam occultata erat, et non consecutus sum ex ea nisi extremitatem paruam eius, cum qua adhaeret in ligno suo: et erat sagitta magna ex sagittis arcuum Turcorum, cum ferro leni, in qua non sunt aures.  
And I extracted another arrow for a Jew, which had lodged in the fat of his eye beneath the lower eyelid, and the arrow was already hidden, and I only managed to reach a small part of it, where it was fixed in its wooden shaft, and it was a large arrow from the Turkish bows, with a smooth iron head, without barbs.

Sanatus est ergo Iudaeus, et non accidit in oculo eius accidens malum.  
Thus the Jew was healed, and no bad incident occurred to his eye.

Et extraxi sagittam aliam ex gutture Christiani.  
And I extracted another arrow from the throat of a Christian.

Et erat sagitta arabica, et est illa cui sunt aures.  
And it was an Arabic arrow, one that has barbs.

Secui ergo super ipsam inter duas guidegi: et iam submersa erat in gutture eius.  
I therefore made an incision over it between the two guidegi, for it was already embedded in his throat.

Subtiliatus sum ergo cum ea, donec extraxi eam: et sanatus est Christianus.  
So I proceeded delicately with it until I extracted it, and the Christian was healed.

Et extraxi sagittam aliam uiro quae ceciderat in uentre eius: et cogitauimus, quia moreretur ex ea.  
And I extracted another arrow from a man, which had fallen into his abdomen, and we thought he would die from it.

Postquam ergo praeterierunt ei triginta dies, et non mutatum est super eum aliquid ex dispositionibus eius, secui super sagittam: et ingeniaui super eam, et extraxi eam: et sanatus est, et non accidit ei accidens malum.  
But after thirty days had passed, and nothing in his condition had changed, I made an incision over the arrow, maneuvered skillfully, extracted it, and he was healed, with no bad incident occurring.

Et uidi uirum cui cecidit sagitta in dorso eius, et consolidatum est uulnus super eam.  
And I saw a man into whose back an arrow had fallen, and the wound had healed over it.

Postquam ergo fuit post septem annos, exiuit sagitta in radice coxae eius.  
Then, seven years later, the arrow emerged at the base of his hip.

Et uidi mulierem cui cecidit in uentre suo sagitta, et consolidatum est uulnus super eam, et remansit sagitta intra ipsam: et non mutata est ex dispositionibus eius aliqua, et mulier non inuenit ei nocumentum in aliqua ex operationibus suis naturalibus.  
And I saw a woman into whose abdomen an arrow had fallen, and the wound healed over it, and the arrow remained inside her, yet none of her bodily functions were affected, and she experienced no harm in any of her natural operations.

Et uidi uirum alium, cui cecidit sagitta in facie sua: et consolidatum est uulnus, et remansit, non inueniens ei multum dolorem: et similia istis multa.  
And I saw another man into whose face an arrow had fallen; the wound healed, and it remained without causing him much pain, and many other similar cases.

Et extraxi sagittam uiro ex principibus Regis, quae ceciderat ei in medio nasi sui, et iam declinauerat ad partem dextram parumper: et occultata erat sagitta tota.  
And I extracted an arrow from a man among the King’s nobles, which had fallen into the middle of his nose and had shifted slightly to the right; the entire arrow was concealed.

Vocatus sum ergo ad curationem eius post casum sagittae usque ad tres dies.  
Thus I was called to treat him three days after the arrow had fallen.

Inueni ergo uulnus sagittae strictum ualde.  
I found the arrow wound very tight.

Inquisiui ergo eam cum tenta subtili, et non sensi eam: et ipse quidem inueniebat punctionem et dolorem sub aure sua ex parte dextra.  
I therefore probed it with a thin probe, and did not feel it, but he did feel a prick and pain under his right ear.

Speraui ergo, quod erat illa punctio ex extremitate sagittae.  
I then suspected that this prick was from the arrow’s tip.

Emplastraui ergo locum cum emplastro in quo erat uirtus attractiua, et digestiua, confidens apud me, quod apostemaretur locus, et appareret mihi signum sagittae, ut secarem super eam: et non accidit in loco accidens significans quod sagitta consecuta sit locum.  
So I applied a plaster to the area with attracting and digesting properties, confident that the area would become inflamed, and the sign of the arrow would appear for me to cut over it; yet no indication showed that the arrow had reached that spot.

Assiduaui ergo cum emplastro super eum diebus multis: et non accidit accidens, et consolidatum est uulnus interim: et remansit infirmus de extractione eius spacio dierum, donec sensit sagittam die quodam intra nasum suum.  
So I continued applying the plaster over him for many days; no incident occurred, and the wound healed in the meantime, and he remained untroubled by the extraction for a period of days until one day he felt the arrow inside his nose.

Et narrauit mihi illud.  
And he told me about it.

Posui ergo super illud uulnus medicinam acutam, corrosiuam diebus multis, donec apertum est: et cum tenta tentaui ipsum, et sensi extremitatem sagittae subtilem quae adhaeret in ligno.  
I then applied a sharp, corrosive medicine over the wound for many days until it opened, and I probed it and felt the thin tip of the arrow where it adhered to the wood.

Deinde addidi in apertione uulneris per illam medicinam acutam, donec apparuit nobis uisibiliter extremitas sagittae: et praeteriit mihi cum eo spacium temporis circiter quatuor menses.  
Then I continued to open the wound with that sharp medicine until the tip of the arrow became visible to us, and approximately four months passed with him.

Deinde postquam amplificatum est uulnus, et possible fuit mihi intromittere forcipes in ipsam, et mouere ipsam, et non obediuit ad exitum: tunc non cessaui subtiliare, et ingeniare super eam cum modis ingeniorum, donec coepi super eam die quodam cum forcipibus decenter factis, secundum quod ueniet forma eorum in fine capituli, donec extraxi eam.  
Then, after the wound had widened enough, and it was possible for me to insert forceps into it and move it, though it did not yield to extraction, I did not stop refining and devising methods over it until one day I started on it with forceps properly made, as their form will appear at the end of the chapter, until I extracted it.

Deinde restauraui uulnus.  
Then I restored the wound.

Et medici quidem iudicant, quod cartilago nasi non restauratur.  
And indeed, doctors judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored.

Restauraui ergo ipsam, et consolidatum est uulnus, et sanatus est infirmas sanitate integra: nec nocuit ei aliquid omnino.  
Nevertheless, I restored it, and the wound healed, and the patient recovered fully, with no harm done to him at all.

Et ego narro tibi qualitatem extractionis quarundam sagittarum: ut ponas illud regulam et significationem super illud quod non dixi.  
And I tell you the manner of extracting certain arrows so that you may use it as a rule and guide over what I have not described.

Quoniam partes huius artis et distinctiones earum non comprehenduntur cum narratione: neque comprehendit illud liber, et artifex prudens comparat cum pauco super multum: et cum eo quod est paesens, super illud quod est absens: et inuenit operationem nouam, et instrumentum nouum apud descensus rerum extranearum huius artis quando accidunt.  
For the parts of this art and their distinctions are not fully conveyed in narration, nor does a book cover it all, and a skilled craftsman compares the small over the large, and what is present over what is absent, and finds a new procedure and new instrument in the context of extraordinary occurrences in this art when they happen.

Dico ergo, quod sagittae non egrediuntur ex membris quibus sunt fixae, nisi secundum duos modos.  
Therefore, I say that arrows do not exit from the parts in which they are fixed except in two ways.

Aut per attractionem ex loco ex quo intrauit.  
Either by drawing it out from the place where it entered.

Aut contrario partis alterius.  
Or through the opposite side.

Et illa quae egreditur unde intrauit, aut est sagitta procedens in loco carnoso: et attrahitur, et egreditur.
And the one that exits from where it entered, or is an arrow lodged in a fleshy area, can be drawn out and extracted.

Quod si non obedit ad exitum ex hora in qua cadit: tunc oportet ut dimittas ipsam aliquot diebus, donec putrefiat caro quae est in circumitu eius: et alleuietur attractio eius, et eius egressio.
But if it does not yield to exit at the time it falls, then you should leave it for a few days, until the flesh around it begins to decompose, and the extraction and removal become easier.

Et similiter si figitur in osse, et non obedit tibi ad exitum, tunc dimitte ipsam etiam aliquot diebus: et itera eam cum attractione et motione omni die, donec egreditur.
Similarly, if it is lodged in the bone and does not yield to you for removal, then leave it also for a few days, and try again each day with traction and movement until it exits.

Quod si non obedit tibi ad exitum post dies, tunc oportet ut perfores in circumitu sagittae in ipso osse ab omni parte cum terebro subtili, donec amplificentur sagittae.
But if it still does not yield to exit after days, then you must drill around the arrow in the bone from all sides with a fine drill, until the area for the arrow is widened.

Deinde attrahe eam, et extrahe ipsam.
Then pull it and extract it.

Si autem sagitta est fixa in capitis osse, et iam processit in uno uentrium cerebri, et apparent ex infirmo quaedam illorum accidentium quae dixi: tunc abstine ab attractione sagittae, et dimitte eam, donec aequetur esse eius post dies.
If, however, the arrow is fixed in the bone of the head and has already entered one of the brain’s ventricles, and some of the symptoms I mentioned appear in the patient, then refrain from pulling the arrow and leave it, until the condition stabilizes after some days.

Nam si sagitta peruenit ad sifach, tunc mors non prolongatur ei.
For if the arrow reaches the membrane (sifach), then death is not delayed for him.

Et si sagitta non est fixa, nisi in corpore ossis tantum, et non penetrat usque ad sifach: et remanet infirmus aliquot diebus, et non accidit ei ex illis accidentibus aliquid: tunc ingenia in attractione sagittae et extractione eius.
But if the arrow is only fixed in the bone itself, and does not penetrate to the membrane, and the patient remains stable for some days without any of those symptoms occurring, then proceed with ingenuity in pulling and extracting the arrow.

Si autem est fixa ualde, et non obedit tibi ad attractionem: tunc administra terebella in circumitu sagittae, sicut narraui tibl: deinde cura locum, donec sanetur.
If it is firmly fixed and does not yield to traction, then use drills around the arrow as I told you, and then treat the area until it heals.

Si autem Sagitta iam absconsa est in loco corporis, et occultatur et absconditur a sensu: tunc inquire eam cum tenta.
If the arrow is already hidden in a part of the body and is concealed and out of reach, then locate it with a probe.

Si autem sentis eam, tunc attrahe eam cum quibusdam instrumentis quae conueniunt attractioni eius.
